Current Affairs Commentary

Will There Be a British-Japanese Compromise? 21

— Hui

㈠ What is the Truth About the British-Japanese Compromise?

"The 'Millard's Review' commented on the secret Anglo-French agreement with Japan, saying, '...Britain and France are clearly concerned about their huge interests in Shanghai. The Japanese attack has greatly damaged these interests. Therefore, they are willing to allow Japan to act freely in Manchuria if they withdraw from Shanghai...' This kind of assertion, coming from the mouth of an American, seems to inevitably have some emotional elements. Before the facts are proven, one dare not be certain that it is the truth. However, the London Times of the 13th of this month actually called the conditions of neutrality proposed by Japan a 'spirit of compromise.' This cannot but arouse suspicion. Yesterday's newspaper had briefly discussed this. From the January 28 Incident in 1932 to the present, one year has passed. The results of the League of Nations' investigation have not provided an appropriate and forceful solution to the issue of the occupation of the Northeast. It has dragged on to this day, and the League of Nations has no power to restrain Japan, nor does it intend to restrain Japan. Therefore, the compromise proposal drafted by the Committee of Nineteen still states in the first item of the first resolution that 'the first task of the League of Nations is to strive to mediate disputes, and the current situation... has not yet reached the stage of offering advice containing facts about the dispute and solutions...' Japanese militarism used force without cause. One hundred thousand iron cavalry trampled on the three provinces. It has been a year and four months now. Are the members of the League of Nations unaware of this? On New Year's Eve this year, they bombarded Shanhaiguan again. Now they have broken through the nine gates, occupied Rehe, and are eyeing Tianjin and Beiping. How can it be said that 'it has not yet reached the stage of offering advice containing facts about the dispute...'? I don't know how it must be before it can be called a 'fact of dispute.' Examining the inside story, it is not about the nature of the dispute, but about what tacit understanding exists between Britain and Japan."

㈡ Economic Relations Between China and Britain

The Japanese army invaded the Northeast, creating the so-called "national self-determination" and establishing a puppet state that is neither fish nor fowl. They proclaimed to the world that their intention was to prevent the southward invasion of Red Russia and to be a Great Wall of capitalism in East Asia. Britain also believed that this was necessary to protect India's security, prevent chaos in China, and consolidate its interests in China for the long term. Little did they know that Japan's "continental policy" is insatiably greedy. In the past, they only spoke of the economic interests of Liaoning and Jilin. Last year, they invaded northern Manchuria, reaching Jinzhou and Yi County. This year, they have captured Yuguan and intend to reach Rehe in the east. If Japan's aggression succeeds, how can the interests of the Beining Railway be guaranteed? Can the Kailuan Coal Mine be enjoyed for a long time? Not only that, but the North China market will probably become the second Manchuria. The economic power of the British will probably be completely driven out.

What is even more serious is that China has many things that need to be developed with foreign capital. China and Britain have also been called friendly. British investment in China exceeds 253.2 million pounds. There is still great hope for the future, because China needs capital and Britain has idle capital. However, Japan has been taking advantage of the European War over the past 20 years and using the political chaos in our country to stir up trouble everywhere. Its investment in China has also reached 2.5 billion yen. Except for railway investment, which is not as large as Britain's, its financial capital and light industrial construction in the Yangtze River and North China are superior to Britain. If we add the support of political power and the forceful disposal of military power, then the old British Empire will probably seek safety but get harm instead.

Moreover, the Japanese government is unusually cunning and has a reputation for having a double-edged diplomacy. Recently, they have been advocating the Monroe Doctrine of East Asia. In the South China region and in India, they are trying their best to express goodwill to the local people, trying to buy them off and help them gain independence in order to carry out their ambition of economic aggression and political development. One wonders why Britain recognizes the enemy as a friend.

㈢ Misunderstanding of Tacit Agreement with Japan

The British clearly understand the advantages and disadvantages and know the difference between right and wrong. They still have some sympathy for the national movement in India and are trying to achieve peace between Britain and India.

Although China has been weak for a long time, the people, after the chaos, are seeking survival in the midst of death and are striving to exist. They will never succumb to the violence of Japan. In the future, they will work harder to regenerate themselves, hoping to contribute to the world. With the strength of 400 million people, they will surely be able to save themselves. The British should have a clear and thorough understanding of this. First, they should recognize that the current China is making rapid progress and is definitely not comparable to 20 or 30 years ago. Second, they should recognize that if China fully achieves its ideal construction and fully develops its industries, it will not only be harmless to Britain, but there will also be a lot of economic mutual benefit. Third, they should recognize that China's struggle against Japan is a matter of life and death for the nation. If Japan immediately abandons its policy of aggression, then peace in East Asia can be permanently guaranteed. If Britain unfortunately helps Japan and suppresses China, thinking that it can seek temporary peace, the result will be the opposite. After Japan annexed the Northeast, the whole situation in East Asia has been shaken. If they invade North China again, China will be transformed into a battlefield, and how much of world peace can be maintained? Fourth, they should recognize that the Chinese people are diligent, hardworking, and have a strong endurance that is difficult for other nations in the world to match. If they are forced to engage in a death struggle, they will not hesitate to continue for generations. A century of national hatred has been forged between China and Japan, which is not a blessing for the future of world peace.

At this time, Britain should be absolutely neutral and should not accommodate the evil facts created by Japan's military force and fuel its ferocity, making the East Asian dispute increasingly incomprehensible and delaying it until it harms world peace and damages Britain's own interests. Do not mistakenly believe that the Chinese are foolish in their forbearance and that the Japanese can be trusted in their hypocrisy.

Gunfire Heard Along the Shi River at Night

Japanese Planes Drop Bombs at Shimenzhai, Over Ten Thousand Puppet Troops Gather at Lijiapu 22

Linyu: Although the front lines have been quiet for the past few days, the situation is still extremely tense and could erupt at any moment. Gunfire is heard along the Shi River at night, and both sides are heavily guarded. Over two hundred enemy artillerymen are guarding the Jiukou Pass, but they show no signs of advancing. The enemy has increased the number of infantry and artillery in Lijiapu and Tiefuchang outside the pass, and there are also seven aircraft stationed at an airfield. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) At 7:00 AM this morning, over one hundred enemy plainclothes troops and thirty Japanese cavalrymen were discovered at Huangtuying, east of the Shi River. They attempted to launch a surprise attack on our defense lines, but our troops opened fire and the enemy fled. At 10:00 AM, four tanks charged towards the Shi River, but our trench artillery shelled them and they retreated towards Yuguan City. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) There was a small engagement at Shimenzhai this morning. Four enemy bomber planes and four explosive planes flew over our positions at 9:00 AM and dropped over ten bombs along the way. Five bombs did not explode. Jiukou Pass is still at a stalemate. Puppet troops are concentrating at Lijiapu, numbering over ten thousand men. Cheng Guorui is serving as the commander-in-chief of the puppet army's First Army Corps, and the headquarters will be moved from Suizhong to the front lines. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) There were no battles along the Shi River and Shimenzhai front lines on the 16th. In the afternoon, three enemy planes scouted between Jiukou Pass and Shimenzhai and dropped bombs, but all missed their targets and we suffered no losses. At night, the Japanese army only fired a few shells as a show of force. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Over one thousand troops from the rebel army of Zhang Bi, outside Jiukou Pass, shelled our positions inside the pass yesterday and were repelled by our artillery fire. The enemy at Yong'anbao had contact with the volunteer army yesterday, and most of the enemy concentrated at Changshantun, awaiting reinforcements. Over one thousand troops from the traitor Li Jichun's forces arrived at Qiansuo and appear to be entering the pass. Residents of Yuguan are moving to the vicinity of the French, British, and foreign military camps. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Two more Japanese warships arrived at Qinhuangdao last night, carrying a large amount of munitions and supplies. Part of them have been transported to the Japanese barracks for storage. Our troops on the Shi River front line are still firmly defending the west bank, while the enemy is stationed at Jiaoshan and the Zhaocao Camp area on the east bank of the Shi River, building defensive works manned by puppet troops. This morning, the enemy commanded over twenty plainclothes troops from the puppet army to harass our positions, but they were repelled by our sentry posts. Our troops at Shimenzhai are still holding the Xiangshui positions, and there has been no contact in recent days. Because of the severe cold, enemy planes outside the pass have not been active in the past two days. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Japanese army plans to pressure our army to near Luan County. When the Yuguan incident occurred, they thought our army would retreat with one blow, but unexpectedly, the resistance has lasted for a full ten days. The enemy is now transferring the newly formed Jing'an Detachment and the newly formed army corps of Zhang Bi, Zhang HaiPeng, Yu Zhishan, and others, along with puppet police, to concentrate at Yuguan. According to statistics in Yuguan, Suizhong, Xingcheng, and Jinzhou, the Japanese army has one division stationed in the area, ready to be deployed for guerrilla warfare at any time. Our army has sufficient forces near Shimenzhai, and there is no concern for defense. The enemy is east of the Shi River Bridge, while we are west of the river, forming a stalemate. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) There is no battle on the Shi River front line today. The Japanese army has only two regiments, about 1,500 men, from Yuguan to the Shi River front line. From Yuguan to Suizhong, there are about two Japanese divisions. The enemy cavalry brigade is currently stationed outside Jiukou Pass at Qiansuo. Except for a small number of Japanese troops stationed at Lijiapu, the rest are rebel troops. Currently, the Japanese are focusing on the Jinzhou-Chaoyang line, and most of the Japanese troops are actively being transported to the Rehe border. The situation in Rehe is very tense. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Japanese army has deployed two fake divisions between Suizhong and Yuguan, the Sixth Division and the Eighth Division. There is also a cavalry brigade stationed in the Qiansuo area. At Jiukou Pass and Lijiapu, there is a battalion of Zhang Bi's puppet troops, and the Japanese army also has an equivalent number. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) There is heavy snow inside and outside the pass, and the temperature has dropped to minus 20 degrees Celsius. Many enemy soldiers are dying and getting sick from the cold. Tanks and machine guns cannot be used, and enemy planes have also stopped operating. There was no battle at Shimenzhai on the 17th, the Shi River is calm, there are no enemy ships at Tanggu, and the area is peaceful. (17th, Special Dispatch)

Japanese Army Attacks Our Nanling Positions

Our Army Responds Calmly, the Front Lines Remain Unchanged, the Volunteer Army Attacks Along Three Routes to Open Up the Datong Road 23

(Beiping) Tang Yulin reported to Beiping this morning that at 1:00 PM on the 16th, Japanese armored vehicles from Chaoyang Temple suddenly shelled our Nanling positions with heavy artillery for half an hour. The Third KenSei Division of the Japanese army began to concentrate and launch an attack on Rehe. There was also contact at Kairu. Details are being investigated. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) A long-distance phone report from Chengde states that over one hundred men from the Third KenSei Division of the Japanese army opened fire on our Nanling positions at noon on the 16th and simultaneously charged our positions. There are three Japanese armored vehicles at Nanling. We responded calmly, and the front lines remained unchanged. Three Japanese planes flew to Balihanziza in the KaiPing County and dropped three bombs, but there were no casualties among our soldiers and civilians. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Volunteer troops from a certain unit in Suizhong engaged in fierce fighting with the enemy in a certain area on the border between Liaoning and Rehe on the evening of the 15th. The enemy used heavy artillery and planes to threaten and bombard them. The volunteer troops are now advancing northwest towards Suizhong. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The volunteer army of Feng Zhanhai and the forces of Li Haiqing, Shi Dianqing, Gao Rongjiu, Guo Chengdong, and others have united and are attacking along three routes to open up the Datong Road. They have been engaged in fierce fighting with the Japanese army in the Beisanjia and Heilinzi areas on the Rehe border for several days. The Japanese are transporting troops from Datongchu Mountain to reinforce Tongliao and will attack Kairu from northern Rehe. The situation in northern Rehe is tense. Japanese planes flew low reconnaissance missions over the Chaoyang Beipiao Qinghe area on the 15th. Japanese armored vehicles have been shelling Chaoyang Temple to provoke trouble for days. The Japanese army has set up a supply station at Dayagou in Jinxi, and a large number of supplies are being stockpiled there. Over one thousand men from the rebel army of Cheng Guorui are stationed at Huolianzhai, thirty-five li east of Beizhangyingzi, and plan to harass Lingyuan. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) In the middle of this month, the enemy launched a joint attack with planes, heavy artillery, and tanks on our defensive positions in the Wangjiayoufang area of Kairu. After a heroic resistance by a certain brigade of the volunteer army of Feng Zhanhai, they fought fiercely for three days and nights and finally repelled the enemy. They are now firmly holding our original defensive positions, building defensive works, and replenishing ammunition. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The main forces of the Japanese Eighth, Sixth, and Fourth Divisions have been concentrating on the Kairu and Chaoyang areas on the Rehe border along the Jinzhou-Chaoyang and Datong roads for days, together with the puppet army. Part of the Fourth Division has been moved from Suizhong and Yuguan to gather at the Great Wall, Shimenzhai, and Jiukou Pass. The volunteer armies of Feng Zhanhai, Zhu Jiqing, and others near Lingyuan on the Rehe border and Kairu and Chaoyang have decided to launch a joint attack on the enemy's base areas of Yixian and Tongliao in the near future as a preemptive measure. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Wang Yunping, commander-in-chief of the National Salvation Army on the Rehe border, sent a telegram to the whole country, urging everyone to make persistent efforts and actively resist in order to achieve the goal of saving the country and the race. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) On the morning of the 16th, the enemy transported two trainloads of soldiers from the South Manchuria Railway in Shenyang, including one thousand Korean soldiers and over ten tanks. In the afternoon, they were transferred to the pseudo Fengshan Railway and got off at the Dahushan Station. They will be split up and sent to the Liaoning-Rehe border and Tongliao. There are over ten Japanese planes parked at each of the two airfields outside the East Gate of Shenyang and at Lanjuntun. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) By order of Mutō, commander of the Japanese Kwantung Army, the pseudo Fengshan Railway and the Shenyang-Jihai railways have dispatched forty trainloads of soldiers, concentrating them at HuangguTuan in Shenyang. It is said that they are transporting troops westward. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to Japanese news, the Japanese army, which is about to attack Rehe, has decided to postpone the invasion until early March due to the weather and international relations. Our official observation is that the Japanese invasion of Rehe is expected, but we are determined to resist to the death and will not risk a rash action. It has always been Japan's policy to invade when we are weak and to change course when we are strong. The Shanghai and Yuguan incidents were both reversals. Although the strength of China and Japan is different, we can endure the pain of defeat, while Japan will collapse if it encounters setbacks. In short, we are determined to resist and will eventually find a way out. (17th, Central News Agency)

(Beiping) People from Tongliao said that a rumor suddenly spread in Tongliao last week that the Chinese government would send planes to bomb Tongliao, causing Japanese merchants in the city to panic and flee. However, Chinese merchants are extremely eager for the national army to go there. (17th, Special Dispatch)

Ma Su Still in Tomsk

Attends Grand Review, Delivers Speech to Russian Army, Report on Japanese Atrocities Has Been Sent Out 24

(Rumor of Ding Chao's Capture Unconfirmed

Potential Strength of Volunteer Army Still Enormous)

(Nanjing) Ma Su has retreated to Russia and is still in Tomsk. It is said that the government has remitted hundreds of thousands of dollars to allow Ma Su and his troops to return to China. Li Du has retreated to Russia and has arrived in Khabarovsk, where he will meet with Ma Su. Although Ding Chao's whereabouts are still unknown, the Japanese report that Ding has been captured is inaccurate. Although the Northeast Volunteer Army has been temporarily quiet due to the departure of its leaders and weather conditions, its potential strength is enormous and will rise up to resist Japan when the green cornfields appear. (17th, Central News Agency)

(Beiping) He Shengda, secretary-general of Su Bingwen, issued a cold telegram from Omsk, stating that Su's report on Japanese atrocities has been completed. The book contains eight chapters and thirty-six sections, detailing the conspiracies and atrocities of the Japanese army in the Northeast from the September 18th Incident to the present. It was sent to the Chinese delegation in Geneva on the 11th for submission to the League of Nations. Karahan recently telegraphed Su, saying that the funds remitted by the Chinese government have arrived and will be allocated immediately. Su and Ma have decided to return to China with important military officers and soldiers due to the urgency of the Yuguan and Rehe situation. They are studying the route through Xinjiang or Outer Mongolia and will be able to leave soon. The refugees who entered Russia with them will remain in Russia temporarily due to insufficient funds. Currently, both the government and the people in Soviet Russia feel tense. Factories are working day and night, and the army is intensifying its exercises. Russian newspapers are advocating that China should declare war on Japan. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) On the 10th, Su Bingwen was invited by the Omsk Labor Club to give a speech, saying that the success of the first five-year plan in Soviet Russia was the result of everyone's hard work, but they should not be optimistic because there are imperialists who are jealous of this success and are constantly provoking incidents. He hoped that everyone would continue to maintain their past spirit, reduce consumption, and increase production in order to fight the invaders in the future. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Chinese people in Beiping do not believe the rumors in Harbin that Ding Chao was captured by Japanese soldiers. According to Ding's representative in Beiping, Ding fled to Russian territory when the Japanese army attacked Suifenhe and is now meeting with General Su Bingwen and others in Omsk. Japanese officials in Beiping have not received any news about Ding Chao's whereabouts, so they cannot confirm the capture. (17th, Reuters)

(Beiping) On the 12th, a grand review of the Russian army was held in Omsk. The Russian side invited Su Bingwen, Ma Zhanshan, and others to attend and give speeches. In addition to praising the Russian army, Su said that Japanese imperialists are trying to create an Asian empire and are willing to destroy world peace and invade China. Everyone must know that invading China is the first step for Japan to rule Asia. He also said that Japan is colluding with a certain country, and its ferocity is increasing. Although the direct conflict is with China today, the indirect conflict is with Soviet Russia. Everyone should be a god of peace and punish those who destroy peace. Finally, he said that "lips are gone, teeth are cold" is the best analogy for China and Russia. If Soviet Russia helps China, it is equal to Soviet Russia saving itself. (17th, Special Dispatch)

About One Thousand Japanese Soldiers Stationed in Qinhuangdao 25

(Beiping) On the afternoon of the 16th, two Japanese ships arrived at the Qinhuangdao pier and unloaded over five hundred Japanese soldiers, who landed at the Dongxin River and were stationed in the seaside Japanese barracks. According to statistics, there are about one thousand Japanese soldiers in Qinhuangdao. The commander of the Second Fleet, Admiral Isaku, is stationed on the ship to command. The Japanese naval operations are mostly concentrated in Huludao. If military action occurs, they can be deployed at any time. One cruiser and two destroyers are dispatched daily to patrol the sea. (17th, Special Dispatch)

He Zhuguo Assumed the Position of Commander of the Third Army Yesterday

The Military Situation on the Front Lines is Extremely Orderly 26

(Beiping) He Zhuguo assumed the position of commander of the Third Army this morning. In addition to continuing to lead the Ninth Brigade, the Third Cavalry Brigade and the Fifteenth Brigade are also under his command. (17th, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) A gentleman who returned from Qinhuangdao after observing the war talked about how orderly the military situation on the front lines is and how supplies are piled up like mountains. He Zhuguo has ordered that they be distributed equally to the combat brigades. He said, "I have dedicated myself to the country. The defense is solid, and the morale of the army is very stable. I am determined to have a grasp of the war." Because he was ordered by the central government, he could not make a statement casually. While he was speaking, a scout reported that several enemy tanks were attacking us. He replied, "Our army is ready," and looked calm. Then he went to visit the trenches and saw that the soldiers were in great need of ear muffs, leather coats, trousers, woolen lining, cotton shoes, and other items, and hoped that compatriots would generously donate. (16th, Special Dispatch)

Qinghua University Female Students Comfort Frontline Soldiers 31

In reality, they contain a miniature image of the entire nation revering you. What an honor!" During the speeches, all the soldiers were eager to fight and shouted to swear to avenge the country and fight to the death for the nation. They were extremely excited. (16th Special Dispatch)

Beiping Citizens Propose Building Cellars Along City Walls 32

In the event of enemy air raids, citizens could take refuge in the cellars to calm the public and secure the rear defenses. The municipal government is currently reviewing this proposal. (17th Special Dispatch)

The Southwest Authorities Telegraph the National Government Urging a Definite Anti-Japanese Stance

Please Expedite the Allocation of Military Supplies and Pay 33

(Hong Kong) The Southwest Political Council telegraphed the Central National Government again on the 17th, stating that they had telegraphed on the 4th, calling for the nation to rise up in resistance against Japan, and telegraphed again on the 6th, urging the government to address four issues. Although a reply was received, the Central Government had not clearly indicated any concrete anti-Japanese strategies. Since the fall of Yu, Japanese aggression has intensified. Calls for resisting Japan and saving the nation have spread far and wide from all provinces, and Yan Gu and others have also telegraphed, urging the government to thoroughly resist Japan. This shows that the people at home and abroad share a unified spirit of resisting Japan. Given the international situation, survival is impossible without resisting Japan. Currently, Rehe is on the verge of collapse, and Beiping and Tianjin are in imminent danger. It is requested that the government quickly express a definite anti-Japanese stance, and expedite the allocation of military supplies and pay to the front-line troops to alleviate the anxieties of the people, rectify international perceptions, and inspire the nation to jointly avert the crisis. If you continue to be unrepentant, harming the country and the people, the Southwest will have no choice but to unite with comrades in all provinces and the people of the nation to shoulder this responsibility, to advance the difficult task of national resistance against Japan. As long as there is breath, we cannot bear to see the loss of an inch of national territory. How will you decide, and please inform us clearly. A warning telegram to Zhang Xueliang is being drafted. (17th Special Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) The Southwest Political Affairs Conference telegraphed Nanjing this afternoon, advocating active action against Japan, with strong wording, including: "If the National Government still does not understand the danger of the overall situation and invites disaster for the country and the people, the Southwest will have no choice but to unite with comrades in all provinces and the people of the nation to take over the work of resisting Japanese aggression. As long as there is breath, we cannot bear to see the loss of an inch of national territory," and other similar statements. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

The Legislative Yuan Held Its First Discussion Meeting Yesterday 34

Decision on the Number of Committee Members and Committee Chairpersons

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its first discussion meeting of the third session on the 17th. Sixty-six members, including Liu Jingxin, attended. Sun Ke chaired the meeting, with Liang Hancao as Secretary-General and Chen Haicheng and Shi Taipu as Secretaries. As a result of the discussion, it was decided to allocate the number of members and chairpersons for the five committees: (1) Legislative Committee: Jiao Yitang, Zhang Zhiben, Lü Zhiyi, and 36 others, with Jiao Yitang as Chairperson; (2) Foreign Affairs Committee: Chuan Bingchang, Lou Tongsun, and 9 others, with Chuan Bingchang as Chairperson; (3) Finance Committee: Ma Yinchu, Liu Guanxun, and 15 others, with Ma Yinchu as Chairperson; (4) Economic Committee: Wu Shangying, Ma Chaojun, and 15 others, with Wu Shangying as Chairperson; (5) Military Affairs Committee: Chen Zhaoying and 15 others, with Chen Zhaoying as Chairperson. It was also tentatively decided to hold general meetings every Friday morning and to assign seating in the conference hall. The list of members for the Criminal Law and Various Regulations Drafting Committee of the Legislative Yuan will be decided at the first general meeting on the 20th. As for the Constitution Drafting Committee, due to its important nature, Sun highly valued the specific organizational methods and selection of members, which will be determined after the first general meeting. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan is scheduled to hold its first general meeting on the 20th. Future meetings will be held every Friday. The Constitution Drafting Committee can be established in the near future. A special committee will also be formed to revise the criminal law and formulate labor laws, and will be specifically responsible for this task. (17th Special Dispatch)

Executive Yuan Resolutions

Appoint Jiang Dingwen as Director-General of the Yangtze River Water Police; Appoint Yu Jichuan, Provincial Committee Member of Hunan Province, Concurrently as Director of Construction 35

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its eighty-third meeting on the 17th. Chen Shuren, Shi Qingyang, Luo Wengan, Liu Ruiheng, Zhu Jiahua, Song Ziwen, and Chen Shaokuan attended. Chen Yi, Zou Lin, Guo Chuntao, Gan Naiguang, Shi Ying, Yu Feipeng, Zeng Zhongming, Chu Minyi, Peng Xuepei, and Duan Xipeng, Zheng Tianxi were present as observers. Song Ziwen chaired the meeting. The resolutions are as follows:

(1) The resignations of Zeng Jiwu and Ye Kaixin, members of the Hunan Provincial Government, were approved. Tan Changkai, a member of the Provincial Committee and concurrently Director of Construction, was relieved of his concurrent position. Yu Jichuan, a member of the Provincial Committee, was appointed concurrently as Director of Construction. Ling Zhang and Huang Jiasheng were appointed as members of the Provincial Government.

(2) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs' request to appoint Rong Jingfang and eight other officers as regimental commanders, brigade commanders, and chiefs of staff of the 82nd Division was approved.

(3) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs' report that Feng Xingzhi, deputy division commander of the 33rd Division, should be officially appointed as lieutenant general and division commander of the division was approved.

(4) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs' report that Tang Yunshan, concurrently commander of the Anqing Garrison, should be dismissed and replaced by Zhang Lühe was approved.

(5) Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Education's report that Li Yan of the Department of Social Education should be dismissed and replaced by Zhang Jiong was approved.

The Course of Russo-Japanese Negotiations on Non-Aggression Treaty

Russia States It Maintains a Peaceful Policy, Proposes a Treaty; Japan Thinks the Time Is Not Ripe, Ambitions Clearly Revealed 73

(Moscow) TASS released today the official documents regarding the Japanese-Russian negotiations for signing a non-aggression treaty. The full text is as follows:

"On December 13, 1932, the Japanese Foreign Ministry verbally conveyed to Soviet Ambassador to Japan, Troyanovsky, the Japanese government's response to the Soviet proposal to sign a non-aggression treaty. The Soviet proposal was made on December 31, 1931, when Yoshizawa passed through Moscow on his way back to Tokyo to take over as Foreign Minister, by Litvinov on behalf of the Soviet government. In its reply, the Japanese government stated that opinions within Japan were quite divided on the timing of signing such a treaty. Supporters believed that the establishment of a non-aggression treaty could guarantee the proper resolution of future disputes between the two countries. Opponents believed that the possible causes of disputes should be eliminated first, before considering the general issue of signing a non-aggression treaty. The Japanese government also believes that the time for concluding a non-aggression treaty is not yet ripe, and therefore it should first address the various issues that affect the mutual relations between the two countries. The Japanese government indicated that at present, both countries could exchange views and decide on a method to prevent or resolve disputes arising from contact between the two countries' armies peacefully on the spot, such as organizing a joint Japanese-Russian-"Manchukuo" committee to prevent border incidents from occurring. Regarding the Japanese government's rejection of signing a non-aggression treaty, Troyanovsky also sent a reply to the Japanese Foreign Minister on January 4, 1933. Troyanovsky stated that the Soviet government was very pleased with the support of a portion of the Japanese for signing a non-aggression treaty, but regretted that the Japanese government could not adopt this view and held the opposite opinion, as the logical development of this opposing view would inevitably be a complete rejection of the fundamental concept of a non-aggression treaty and the Kellogg-Briand Pact's approach to resolving disputes through international renunciation of war. Troyanovsky also stated that the Japanese government's opinion clearly assumes that a non-aggression treaty can only be signed when there are no points of contention between the two countries. However, in the current state of economic and political interdependence among nations, especially between neighboring countries, it is impossible to have no points of contention. Even if temporary differences are resolved, there is no guarantee that they will not arise again in the future. Furthermore, countries that have already concluded non-aggression treaties with the Soviet Union have not considered themselves to have no mutual points of contention or demands with the Soviet Union in doing so. Recently, the Soviet Union agreed to conclude a non-aggression treaty with a neighboring country that has a border dispute with the Soviet Union and claims sovereignty over a certain territory. Therefore, the Soviet government's view of non-aggression treaties and the Kellogg-Briand Pact is that countries acknowledge the existence of points of contention or the possibility of points of contention arising, but decide to renounce the use of force to resolve such points of contention. On the Soviet government's side, it feels that there are no points of contention between the Soviet Union and Japan that cannot or should be refused to be resolved peacefully. To refuse would contradict the Kellogg-Briand Pact, which was jointly signed by Japan and Russia. The Soviet government's proposal to conclude a non-aggression treaty with Japan is not intended to disregard the Kellogg-Briand Pact, but merely to strengthen it with a bilateral agreement to adapt it to the specific circumstances of the relationship between the two countries. Troyanovsky continued, the Soviet proposal is not based on the current situation, but is based on the Soviet Union's entire peaceful policy, and hopes that it can be maintained for a long time. At the same time, the Soviet government doubts whether one party's refusal to sign a non-aggression treaty is conducive to resolving disputes and eliminating misunderstandings between the two countries. In addition, the Soviet government specifically pointed out that in the Japanese government's verbal reply, there was the phrase "Japan and the Soviet Union are both willing to mutually respect each other's sovereignty and absolutely prohibit infringing on each other's borders," saying that if this intention can be strictly adhered to, then even though Japanese troops are currently approaching the Soviet border, there should not be more border incidents than before. Finally, the Soviet government stated that it is prepared to study and consider the Japanese proposal to organize a joint Japanese-Russian-"Manchukuo" committee, believing that it may be possible to organize a committee similar to those the Soviet Union has with neighboring countries such as Romania and Poland to prevent border disputes. (TASS dispatch on the 17th)"

Content of Saito's Speech to Parliament

Still Claiming to Resolve the Yuguan Incident and Hoping for Close Sino-Japanese Relations? 74

Tokyo, 17th (Japan Allied News) Prime Minister Saito will deliver a policy speech in Parliament on the direction of his administration and other important issues. The recent Yuguan Incident is deeply regrettable in Sino-Japanese relations. The government intends to resolve this issue satisfactorily with sincerity and hopes for close Sino-Japanese relations. ㈡ The 1933 Budget: The Hamaguchi Cabinet implemented an extremely tight fiscal policy. However, since the Manchurian Incident, the domestic and international situations have become serious. Military spending for the army and navy had to be increased, and other important expenses were also expanded. As a result, the budget has become a huge number. ㈢ The large budget poses a dangerous impact on the national finances in the future. The government is currently considering these criticisms, and the Ministry of Finance is also deliberating countermeasures. According to the government's forecast, the Japanese economy will definitely improve between 1933 and 1934. It also believes that the current dilapidated rural areas will be able to return to their original state by 1934. The issue of tax increases will be considered after this recession disappears. ㈣ Efforts to address emergency issues: The government already has considerable measures, but the actions of left and right-wing groups within the country are endless. The government is determined to do its utmost to supervise and guide public opinion and to reform national education. ㈤ Explain the reasons for submitting various bills such as debt consolidation, rice control, pension law revision, and election law revision.

Japanese Military Clique Organizes Fascist Party

Using Retired Soldiers as Core Members 75

Tokyo, 17th (Japan Allied News) After the shocking May 15th Incident, a fascist atmosphere permeated Japan. The fascist political party, the National Alliance (led by Kodama Yoshizo), has already emerged. A conference will be held in Tokyo soon. Its program aims to thoroughly implement imperial rule and to promote the essence of the Japanese national polity. Its purpose is to break the accumulated abuses of existing political parties, establish fair politics, abolish the capitalist economic system, and implement a national controlled economic system.

New Greek Cabinet Formed

Venizelos Appointed Prime Minister 76

Athens, 16th (Reuters) After the resignation of the Theodaris Cabinet on January 13, a new cabinet has now been organized by the 68-year-old prominent politician Venizelos. Venizelos himself serves as Prime Minister, and Kafantaris is appointed Minister of Finance, Michalakopoulos as Minister of Foreign Affairs, and Katachakis as Minister of the Army. During the European War, Venizelos strongly supported the Allied Powers and repeatedly asked King Constantine to join the Allied side, but the King and the General Staff repeatedly deemed it impossible. Venizelos later broke with the King and established a provisional revolutionary government in Salonika. In 1917, King Constantine abdicated, Alexander succeeded him, and Venizelos was summoned back to Tokyo to serve as Prime Minister of the National Government. The victory of the Allied forces in Salonika was largely due to Venizelos's assistance.

Natal, Brazil, 16th (Havas)

At 4:48 PM today (local time, which is 7:20 PM Greenwich Mean Time), the French aircraft "Arc-en-Ciel" flew across the South Atlantic from the French colony of Senegal in Africa and arrived here. The aircraft departed at 4:00 AM this morning and flew for 13 hours, covering a distance of more than 3,000 kilometers.

Natal, Brazil, 16th (Reuters) The French three-engine large aircraft Arc-en-Ciel, flying from France to South America, arrived here at 4:40 PM today, taking four and a quarter days. The aircraft flew out of Marseille at 10:10 AM on January 12. This voyage was very successful. The director of the French airline, Varré-Vela, announced today that the second flight of the Arc-en-Ciel will be of a commercial nature. In about two months, a regular weekly air service will be launched between Paris and the Brazilian capital, with the entire journey from France to South America taking only three days.

Russian Ship in Distress 82

Moscow, 16th (National News Agency) The Russian ship Sakhalin, carrying a total of 284 people, was previously reported to be in distress in the Vodozersky Sea. There has been no news of it so far. There are currently heavy snowstorms, preventing other ships from sailing to rescue it.

Moscow, 17th (National News Agency) According to official announcements, the passengers and crew of the Russian ship Sakhalin all escaped onto ice floes. An icebreaker is currently docked beside them, and another ship is sailing to the scene of the accident to carry out rescue operations.

Japanese 1933 War Budget (Japan News)

Militaristic Policy and Preparation to Attack Russia, Expanded Expenditures and Financial Crisis 83

In recent years, the impoverishment of the working masses in Japan has increased daily. However, the Japanese government's budget for 1933 has revenue of only 1.2 billion yen, while expenditures reach a huge 2.237 billion yen. This shows how the Japanese imperialists are trembling in the face of the crisis of bankruptcy and how they are trying to avoid this terrible crisis. The bulk of the budget revenue comes from taxes (56%) and government industries and assets (36%). Since 1930, fear and poverty have been incessant in Japanese society, making it impossible for the working masses to pay taxes. Moreover, indirect tax payers, who account for 56% of taxes, have also suffered losses in their payments due to the decline in mass purchasing power and the reduction in sales of consumer goods (1931). At the same time, the poverty of the masses has also reduced the profits from monopolies such as tobacco, so revenue has also shown a trend of resentment and decline since 1930. At the same time, the amount of expenditures has had to increase greatly due to the urgency of the war situation. The emergence of the so-called "deficit budget" (surplus budget) has also lasted for three years. However, the unbalance between revenue and expenditure and the fiscal expansion in the 1933 budget are unprecedented.

Regarding the 1933 budget, the government-controlled newspapers said that the reasons for the expansion are three: First, the expansion of military spending; Second, the emergency relief expenses; Third, the expansion of public debt expenses.

(Military Spending) First, military spending refers to the Manchurian Incident expenses and the military preparedness improvement expenses. The Manchurian Incident expenses are allocated for use in Manchuria's defense and security maintenance. No matter how eloquently Matsuoka Yosuke speaks at the League of Nations, the "Manchukuo puppet state" is completely a puppet under the wings of Japanese imperialism. This fact is undeniable. After the Japanese imperialists "created" this puppet state, they also bear such a huge budget for it. The Japanese government was originally a girl in the arms of the warlords, so naturally it does not hesitate to invest a large amount of funds for warlord wars, opening roads, laying railways, and arming Yilan and Fujin in the Songhua River area, preparing for the main road for future wars with the Soviet Union. Moreover, Qiqihar is used as its starting point, passing through the Greater Khingan Mountains, the Outer Mongolian Republic, Hailar, and Manchouli to attack Siberia. However, the Japanese working masses are squeezed out of their own blood tax for the use of this purpose.

Secondly, there are the military preparedness improvement expenses, totaling 290 million yen, of which:

On the Army side:

Enhancement of military strength in Manchuria and reorganization of domestic troops: 138,137,000 yen

Supplementary Education: 9,291,000 yen

Improvement of various short-term emergency systems: 12,092,000 yen

Replenishment and reorganization of combat materials: 87,850,000 yen

On the Navy side:

New warship maintenance fees: 15,195,000 yen

Expenses for air squadrons, aircraft, and other equipment: 15,594,000 yen

Additional amount for warship manufacturing fees: 15,000,000 yen

Warship modification fees: 20,688,000 yen

Military preparedness enhancement and improvement fees: 21,710,000 yen

Army Minister Araki loudly shouted, "We want to conquer the world, and national defense and military preparedness enhancement fees are absolutely indispensable." This sentence has now reached the stage of implementation. If you don't believe it, please see:

The large airfield plan in Toyohara, Sakhalin;

The major modification and armament plan for the national highway from Otomari/Toyohara to the Soviet border;

The Niigata large airfield plan;

The construction of a candidate airfield in Hama-Kurosaki, Toyama Prefecture;

The large construction of Tsuruga Port;

The large-scale reconstruction and large-scale exercises at Maizuru Port;

The implementation of the Tadaumi poison gas factory and air defense facilities in the Kita-Kyushu area in Hiroshima Prefecture;

Reconstruction of Cheongjin Port near the Korean border and development of shipping from Cheongjin Port to Tsuruga;

The Luo Xin large port construction plan;

The layout of the Japan-Korea-Manchuria air network;

The establishment of the Manchuria Aviation Company;

The designation of a candidate airfield in Dongshi Township, Tainan Prefecture, Taiwan;

The expansion of the Jiadong Airfield area;

The construction and reconstruction of long-distance bus roads;

Wireless communication between Taipei and Manila;

The Japan Petroleum Company's plan to increase oil production in Jinshui, etc.

Among the improvements in the treatment of soldiers that have already been implemented are the increase in officers and students, the reorganization of tank squadrons, the establishment of a cadre candidate system and a specialist non-commissioned officer system, and the recent formation of a "warrior" team to suppress the internal turmoil in the army.

This huge amount of military facilities expenses and the most active munitions factories are intertwined, implementing a very high-intensity labor policy for all workers. Since most of the Japanese munitions factories are state-owned institutions, they forcibly implement their military management by using the names of "war" and "emergency" to reject all economic and political demands. He Zhuguo Vows to Fight to the Death

Expressing to the Japanese Representative on the Drafting of the Peace Agreement for Beiping and Saying the Positions Are Solid and Our Army Is Confident 84

Beiping Communication: The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of all circles in Beiping recently sent representatives with more than 40 boxes of wool gloves and other items to Yuguan to comfort the soldiers at the front. The representatives completed their mission on the 12th and returned to Beiping. The details are recorded as follows:

Representatives Inspect the Battlefield 85

Each representative took the Beiping-Liaoning Railway's

8th train east in the morning of the 10th, arriving at Beidaihe at 6 PM. The adjutant Meng Zhengsheng and the quartermaster Zhao, from the 9th Brigade's station office, greeted them at the station and transferred the comfort items to a special train. At the same time, 13 male and female students from the Yanjing University Comfort Group brought items with them. The two groups then joined forces. Because it was too late, they changed their plans to visit Commander He the next morning. At 5 AM the next morning, Commander He sent two military vehicles to the station to pick them up. After traveling about 50 miles to the headquarters, they were warmly received by Adjutant Ding Shilin and others. After the meal, the representatives went to inspect the surrounding area and saw that some trenches had been built, while others were still under construction. Because the weather was very cold, the ground was frozen about one foot deep, so they had to burn firewood until the frozen ground melted before they could work. It was not until 3 PM that they visited Commander He. At this time, the Nankai University Comfort Group also arrived, and the three groups were received at the same time. First, the representative of the Anti-Japanese Association explained the intention of the visit. Then, Commander He delivered a speech of thanks.

Commander He Zhuguo Talks 86

Commander He said in his speech, "I am deeply ashamed of the unfortunate loss of Shanhaiguan this time. I am very grateful for the visit and gifts from the representatives of various groups. I would like to briefly describe the course of the incident. The Japanese army's attack on Shanhaiguan this time did not have a real target. Because Shanhaiguan was bound by the Boxer Protocol, it has been virtually open for 30 years. Since the September 18th Incident, the Japanese have arbitrarily increased troops and deployed defenses under the pretext of the treaty, while we have not been able to increase troops freely. The two armies were originally separated by the Great Wall. Later, the puppet state's military police entered the station within the pass, and from then on, there were increasing troubles. Their intention to occupy Rehe and complete the puppet state's plan was clearly revealed. At the beginning of the incident, I was in Beiping on official business, and the Japanese army tried their best to create rumors and provocations, while we tried to seek perfection. We also told the Japanese that all problems would be resolved after I returned to defense. The Japanese army could not wait and began to attack, limiting us to allowing four conditions within 50 minutes. I ask you, if we allowed these conditions, it would be better to clearly cede Shanhaiguan, which could save the residents from bloodshed. After I returned to defense, I quickly stepped up the deployment of defenses in various places. Because I was restricted by the Boxer Protocol in advance, I could not increase troops. Increasing troops would be regarded by the Japanese as taking hostile actions, so only three battalions were stationed in the city. The defense project was arranged secretly. The Japanese army advanced on three sides, sea, land, and air. Although our army resisted fiercely, the disparity in weapons and manpower was too great. The Japanese army surrounded the southeast and west cities and set up an artillery position on the northeast corner of the highlands outside the city, bombarding our soldiers defending the city, so that the Japanese army could climb the city. Our army was attacked from both sides, and all four gates were closed. The only way out for our army was the Xicheng Water Gate. However, the Japanese army was already waiting there and used machine guns to strafe, so that the entire battalion was wiped out. It cannot be said that it was not miserable. After our army retreated, the Japanese army thought they could pursue our army to the Luanhe area, so that there would be no worries about advancing into Rehe. Compared to attacking Rehe from the Kailu area, it would be twice as effective. This was the original plan. Unexpectedly, although our army retreated, they immediately consolidated their defenses in the Shihe area and defeated the Japanese army's pursuing team of more than 1,000 people. The reason why the Japanese army failed to enter the Luanhe was the resistance of our army's new defense line. On the evening of the second, a Japanese train drove to Shanhaiguan but did not get off. Later, because the pursuit of our army failed, the Japanese withdrew this train of troops and announced to the world that this was a local issue and that the commander of the Tianjin Garrison would resolve it, separate from the Kwantung Incident, and minimize the scope. The Japanese army sent a letter to me asking to negotiate with them. I have replied that my responsibility from now on is only to defend the territory and that this incident should be resolved by the central government. There is no change in the positions of both sides and they are currently in a stalemate. In short, the defense of the front line is generally undertaken by our army, and we have full confidence. Please rest assured, I am determined to die and then stop, and I will try my best to deal with it.

I don't think there will be any major changes, but the Japanese are full of tricks. If this plan doesn't work, they may expose their hideous face and disrupt other places, or even cause a second world war. This is the awakening that our nation should have and prepare for early. There may be no major war recently, but if there is a war, it will break out in various places at the same time. Soldiers have always regarded dying on the battlefield as their duty, but for all other matters, we cannot but hope that the people will rise up and work together to overcome the national crisis."

Military Personnel's Hands and Feet Frostbitten 87

Reports from various representatives who recently inspected the troops indicated high morale. However, the soldiers, despite having cotton-padded jackets and trousers, lacked leather hats and greatcoats, resulting in many suffering frostbite on their hands and feet. One representative spoke with a soldier and gifted him his own gloves. The soldiers gathered to discuss this, saying that the representatives of various groups were diligently working to deliver donated goods and were confident of defeating the Japanese. After returning to Peiping, the representatives considered winter gear the most pressing need for the soldiers at the front and planned to unite various sectors to raise funds for collecting padded vests, cotton gloves, woolen socks, and other items to send to the front lines in succession. (14th)

Songjiang

Prosecutor's Office Thoroughly Investigates Opium Trafficking in Fengjing 88

Fengjing Town, in the county, sits on the border of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. It is divided by a boundary river, and the urban area is prosperous with thriving commerce. However, since Zhejiang Province strictly prohibited opium, Fengjing became a major outlet. All trafficking operations centered in Songjiang, distributing to nearby areas. The trade was so lucrative that daily sales reportedly reached thousands of taels of silver. The scale was grand, almost like Shanghai's opium dens, with open sales and no fear. These groups transported goods secretly with ingenious methods, and despite investigations, few cases were solved. Recently, the Fourth District Party Branch in the town, noting the near-public sale of opium, telegraphed the Prosecutor's Office for a thorough investigation. Chief Prosecutor Zhu secretly ordered Judicial Police Chief Sheng Dexin to investigate Fengjing covertly, without making a sound, and arrest the culprits when possible. The police chief went yesterday (17th) and visited the District Party Branch to inquire. He learned that after the District Party Branch's report, the opium traffickers, realizing the difficulty of maintaining their operation, had temporarily ceased activities. The main traffickers had also reportedly left the town. Sheng returned to Songjiang to report.

Wuxi

Fuxin Factory Employee Commits Suicide After Being Laid Off 89

Tao Hongshu, a resident of No. 6 Xiaolou Lane in the city, was 36 years old. He worked at the Fuxin Flour Mill in Shanghai. He had an elderly father in his seventies and two brothers. The elder brother, Guanlun, had served as the chief of the Public Security Bureau in Songjiang and Baoying counties. The younger brother, Xingsheng, worked in a flour mill in Tianjin. Hongshu was married to a virtuous woman named Zhu, and they had a very close relationship. Last year, they had a daughter, and the couple was very happy. Unfortunately, Zhu fell ill after childbirth, and despite all treatments, she passed away. Since then, Hongshu suffered from mental confusion, mumbling incoherently. Unexpectedly, the Fuxin factory underwent layoffs last year, and Hongshu was among those laid off. This further aggravated his mental state, and he conceived the idea of suicide. The day before yesterday evening, he went to the Hanchang Road Hotel, booked a room, and then committed suicide by poisoning. The next day, the waiter discovered him, but it was too late to revive him.

Changzhou

Homicide Occurs Near Baizhang 90

A headless male corpse was discovered on the morning of the 15th in Xitangjia Village near Baizhang Town in Wuyi North Township. The head was half-severed between the eyes and ears, and there were knife wounds on both hands, a bloody and gruesome sight. Yu Shiquan, the captain of the First Squad of the town's garrison police, reported the incident and dispatched a team to investigate. He also reported to the county, requesting the County Court Prosecutor's Office to send personnel for an examination. Due to rain and snow-covered roads on the 16th, they could not travel. Today (17th), personnel are being sent to the countryside for investigation.

Xiaoxinqiao Police Squad Captures Robbers 91

Wu Fu's family in Dazhuji Village, Chashu Township, Wuyi 18th District, was recently robbed. Li Jianyi of the garrison police squad in Xiaoxinqiao Town reported the incident and dispatched a team to investigate for several days. At approximately 1:00 PM on the 15th, they coordinated with the local militia to arrest Wang Mingzhang, his elder brother Wang Changda, and Mingzhang's nephew Wang Heshang in Beihuangou Village, Shishu. They recovered twenty to thirty pieces of stolen clothing. The suspects were taken into custody for preliminary interrogation and confessed to an accomplice named Ai Huosheng, who was also subsequently arrested. After the victim identified the stolen goods as belonging to them, the squad leader sent the suspects to the headquarters in the city on the 16th for further interrogation.

Jiangyin

Labor Union Extortion Involved Party Committee 92

In the case of the Shipworkers' Union's extortion under false pretenses, Yao Zhiming, Wu Hengfu, and others were handed over to the county by the water police. On the 14th, Judge Wang Cheng interrogated them. According to Yao and the others, the Shipworkers' Union was organized by Chen Xiping, a member of the County Party Committee, through Zhou Linrong. Due to a lack of funds for the Party Committee, a subsidy of two hundred yuan was required. One hundred yuan was paid on December 17th of last year, with a receipt signed by Chen Xiping, a standing committee member of the County Executive Committee. The remaining one hundred yuan was due on schedule, but they could not comply, so they collected it from the membership registration fees, which was not extortion. The judge sentenced Yao Mingzhi to one month of imprisonment, Wu Hengfu to twenty days of detention and a fine of ten yuan, Yao Baoshen to a fine of ten yuan, and Cao Zhengkun to a fine of twenty yuan.

Yangzhou

Heavy Snow in Yangzhou City 93

Since the beginning of winter, the weather in Yangzhou City has been mild, like early spring. The night before last, a strong northwest wind suddenly blew, and the temperature dropped sharply. By the next morning, heavy snow was falling, continuing throughout the day. By evening, the snow had accumulated to about a foot thick, transforming the entire city into a silver world. The first and last train services between Zhenjiang and Yangzhou were suspended, long-distance telephone lines were also down, the electric lights flickered, and there were very few pedestrians in the streets. Most businesses closed in the afternoon.

In Zhangjiayuan Village, Fourth District, a fire broke out in the home of a farmer surnamed Chen at 3:00 AM the night before last for unknown reasons. The family awoke from their dreams and escaped the fire, but a 24-year-old blind woman and her four-year-old child were unable to escape and perished in the flames. A tragic event.

Letter from Jiangyin Tianlun Dyeing and Weaving Company 95

To the editor of Shen Bao:

We are writing in response to a report in your paper of the 14th regarding "Raising Funds under False Pretenses," which stated that an organization called the Shipworkers' Union had set up an office inside the Tianlun Textile Factory in Shejiaqiao and charged fees to passing ships. This is not in accordance with the facts. This type of union was once found in a thatched hut by the river near our factory, but not set up inside our factory. The content is under official investigation. This factory is related to our reputation and we are specially requesting this correction, in order to avoid false rumors. We await a reply, Tianlun Co., Ltd., January 15th.

Shanghai Branch of the China League for Civil Rights Established Yesterday

Soong Ching Ling and Others Elected as Executive Committee Members 97

The Shanghai branch of the China League for Civil Rights held its inaugural meeting at the Central Research Institute on Albert Road yesterday at 4:00 PM. Cai Yuanpei chaired the meeting, and Zou Taofen served as the recorder. The branch's charter was adopted, and a declaration was issued. Soong Ching Ling, Cai Yuanpei, and nine others were elected as executive committee members. The details of the meeting are as follows:

Members Present 98

The members present at yesterday's meeting included Cai Yuanpei, Yang Xingfo, Lin Yutang, Harold Isaacs, Agnes Smedley, Zou Taofen, Xu Shen, Wu Hanqi, Dong Binhe, Lin Zhongke, Guo Weiran, Hu Yuzhi, Lu Xun, Zhou Jianren, Wang Zaoshi, Zheng Dapu, and others, totaling sixteen individuals.

Meeting Proceedings 99

(1) Adoption of the Branch Charter; (2) Amendment and Issuance of a Declaration; (3) Election of Nine Executive Committee Members; (4) Election of Three Delegates to the National Congress; (5) Nomination of Three Members Each for Publicity, Investigation, and Legal Advisory Committees; (6) Discussion.

Branch Charter 100

Charter of the Branch of the China League for Civil Rights: (1) Cities with more than twenty members may, with the permission of the National League, organize a branch. However, there shall be no more than two branches in the same city. (2) Membership shall be in accordance with the National League's charter. Those who support the National League's aims and are willing to engage in practical work to realize these aims, regardless of nationality, gender, or political belief, may be candidates for membership in the Branch League, nominated by three members and approved by a majority vote of the National League's Executive Committee. The Executive Committee may refuse membership to those who have previously participated in activities that deprive civil rights. (3) There shall be two types of members: individual and group. (4) Individual members shall pay an annual membership fee of three yuan, and group members shall pay an annual membership fee of ten yuan. (5) All members shall have the right to vote and be elected. (6) Each branch may establish a branch executive committee to manage branch affairs. The executive committee shall be composed of five to nine members elected from among the members at the annual general meeting each year. Executive committee members shall serve for a term of one year but may be re-elected. (7) Each branch executive committee may appoint one chairman, vice-chairman, secretary, and treasurer, as well as several staff members, who shall be elected from among the executive committee members. (8) Each branch shall hold an annual general meeting once a year and meet at least once a month. (9) Each branch may establish various committees, such as a prison investigation committee, a legal advisory committee, and a publicity committee, whose members shall be appointed from among the members. (10) Each branch shall elect three delegates to attend the National Committee of the League. (11) Each branch may issue declarations and circulars within the scope of its jurisdiction, provided that they do not violate the aims and charter of the League and are signed by the executive committee members of each branch. (12) Each branch shall report to the National League on facts and work related to civil rights protection within its jurisdiction at any time and shall submit a consolidated report at the end of each month. (13) Two-thirds of the branch's membership fees shall be used for branch expenses, and one-third shall be submitted to the National League for National League expenses. (14) Each branch may raise donations at any time to maintain branch affairs. (15) Amendments to this branch charter may be proposed by the branch and submitted to the National League Executive Committee for discussion and amendment.

Issuance of Declaration 101

Declaration of the Shanghai Branch of the China League for Civil Rights: All struggles to secure political, social, economic, and moral liberties have as their fundamental aim the demand for freedom of speech, freedom of the press, and freedom from forceful interference, the right to express opinions, and the right to freely expose and criticize social forces that hinder the happiness of the majority. The concept of genuine democracy has been the guiding principle of all social struggles for three hundred years, and millions have shed blood for it. To this day, it remains the center of social and economic struggles. However, its effect, if it only extends to a few people, cannot be considered a success. Only when the majority of the people enjoy its benefits can democracy be said to be established. Democracy, as the aim of all forward-looking struggles, is undoubtedly true. However, many forces that impede the progress of humanity often attribute the benefits of democracy to a few while depriving others of their due civil rights. The significance of this struggle is particularly important in China today. While the world's population is suffering a fatal blow from economic hardship, the Chinese people must endure the aggression of Japan and other imperialists in addition to the world's hardship. This threat is deeply ingrained in the minds of the Chinese people. Only when the Chinese people can hold their destiny in their own hands and fight for the survival of the nation can there be hope. However, if the people cannot freely unite and freely express their opinions, they cannot fight for the nation. The future of China completely depends on the Chinese people, and the path lies in achieving freedom of thought, freedom of speech, and freedom of action. Otherwise, China will be reduced to Africa, and there will be no other path to future economic, social, and political development. This undeniable fact is proven not only by pen and tongue but also by the history of iron and blood. However, the Chinese people still have no trace of even the most basic civil rights. On the contrary, magazines and newspapers are often banned, and gatherings and associations are often prohibited. In the past five years, hundreds of publications have been banned or had their postal rights suspended. The content of these magazines and newspapers includes various political views, ranging from the extreme left to the extreme right. Not only are the opinions and criticisms of Chinese authors and many purely artistic publications banned, but publications describing social and cultural struggles abroad are also not allowed to circulate in the country. Even possessing such books is sufficient grounds for imprisonment and execution. Those who suffer this misfortune are not limited to publications that criticize domestic or world conditions. We still remember that the Peiping Daobao and the Minguo Daily (the Kuomintang's official newspaper) were banned due to unreasonable demands from Japanese imperialists. In other words, under the current conditions, even the views of the ruling party cannot be safely expressed. The severity of the prohibitions and the secrecy of the network of restrictions are such that even if the editors of banned magazines and newspapers are spared imprisonment, they do not dare to protest. If China wants to resist enemies, and if the Chinese people want to gradually advance to the realm of genuine democracy, then this gag that prevents new ideas, new criticisms, and freedom of speech must be removed. The China League for Civil Rights is willing to awaken the Chinese people and encourage them to strive to realize the benefits of freedom of publication, freedom of speech, freedom of assembly, and freedom of association, all genuine civil rights, to oppose all censorship and prohibitions, and to awaken the people to demand the universal enjoyment of the minimum civil rights and to stop the oppression of writers, artists, and magazine and newspaper editors who are striving for China's progress and liberation.

Elected Executive Committee Members 102

As a result of the voting election, Soong Ching Ling, Cai Yuanpei, Yang Quan, Lin Yutang, Harold Isaacs, Zou Taofen, Chen Binhe, Hu Yuzhi, Lu Xun, and nine others were elected as executive committee members.

Committee Members of Each Section 103

Following the election, Wang Zaoshi, Wu Hanqi, Yu Zengxia, and three others were nominated as Publicity Committee members. Zhou Jianren, Lin Zhongke, Zhang Zhihan, and three others were nominated as Investigation Committee members. Zhang Zhirang, Guo Weiran, Shen Junru, and three others were nominated as Legal Committee members. Support Association for Volunteer Army Urges Ma Zhanshan and Others to Return Home (Telegram) 105

The Shanghai Support Association for the Northeast Volunteer Army telegraphed the National Government, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday, requesting the transportation of Generals Ma Xiufang, Su Ganzhang, and Wei Zhichu back to China, and also telegraphed Ma Zhanshan and others in Vormesk to quickly reorganize their troops and return to China. The two telegrams are transcribed below:

To the National Government (Telegram): "To the esteemed National Government, Executive Yuan, and Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing: Ma Zhanshan, Chairman of Heilongjiang Province, Su Bingwen, Commander of the Railway Protection Army, and Generals Zhang Dianjiu and Xie Ke, due to exhaustion of ammunition and lack of reinforcements, were unable to continue fighting and retreated into Russian territory. Currently, China and Russia have resumed diplomatic relations, making diplomatic operations easier. Since the government has already remitted funds for relief, immediate steps should be taken to transport Generals Ma, Su, Li, Zhang, and Xie, and the officers and soldiers under their command, back to China, to avoid them staying in a foreign country for too long. Sincerely, Chu Fucheng, Li Cishan, Yin Zhufu, Wu Shan, Feng Shaoshan, Yu Huancheng, Yan Zhifang, Jiang Wenyu, Li Shaochuan, Du Chongyuan, Chen Yafu of the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association, bow."

Telegram to Ma Zhanshan: "To the Chinese Consulate in Siberia, transferred to Chairman Ma Zhanshan and General Su Bingwen in Vormesk, and to inquire with General Li Du: The Northeast has fallen under the aggression of violent bandits. Fortunately, the generals have successively resisted and fought the enemy for the country, achieving immortal feats in a difficult environment. The hand-to-hand combat has lasted for years, shaking the mountains and rivers. Due to the cut-off of foreign aid and the lack of relief, they have retreated with tears. Looking to the north, their hearts are extremely saddened. The national crisis is critical, and the enemy's threat is intensifying. The generals and their officers and soldiers cannot stay in a foreign country for long. Regardless of the difficulty of the journey, in addition to urging the government to quickly take steps to transport them back, this special telegram requests the generals to quickly reorganize and return home to lead the volunteer army again and recover lost territory. The country's future relies on this. Looking forward to your arrival. "

Begging for Prompt Relief and Replenishment to Enable Return to Heilongjiang to Continue Resistance 106

Deng Wen, a hero of the anti-Japanese war in Heilongjiang, has actively replenished his forces after leading his 10,000 men through Rehe. His subordinates and the infantry of Su and Zhang have arrived in Linxi one after another. The costs of telegraphing and other expenses are still unpaid. Please report the blood battles that my troops have fought with the enemy to all authorities and organizations so that prompt relief and replenishment can be provided to enable a return to Heilongjiang to continue resistance. Chairman's son Ma Ziyuan (omitted) can contact and cooperate with you. Deng Wen and Li Shiji bow."

The case has been resolved and submitted to the Political Council for transfer to the Lower House, and a separate order will be issued. I hereby urgently telegraph to order you to strictly comply.' Chinese Taxpayers in the French Concession Request More Chinese Director Seats

Yesterday's Joint Meeting of Executive and Supervisory Committees Proposed 115

The French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association convened a joint meeting of its executive and supervisory committees yesterday. Those in attendance included Du Yuesheng, Shang Mu Jiang, Cheng Zhusun, Jin Tingsun, Zhu Shengmao, Xu Xiuting, Dong Kegong, Qu Zhenhua, Tong Lizhang, Pan Zhaobang, (Cheng Zhusun substituting for) Xi Jingyan, (Xu Xiuting substituting for). Also invited to attend and participate in the discussions were the current Chinese directors of the French Municipal Council, Lu Bohong, Zhang Xiaolin, Zhu Yanzhi, Wei Tingrong, and Qi Yunqing. Du Yuesheng served as chairman, and Tong Lizhang as recorder. The proceedings were conducted with due formality. The proposed matters were as follows: ㈠ The association previously received a letter from citizens stating that the French Water and Electricity Company was planning to increase prices. The association had sent a letter to the Chinese directors urging them to pay attention to this matter. However, the company repeatedly requested the Municipal Council to hold ad hoc meetings a few days ago, demanding the implementation of the price increase. However, the French Consul-General attached great importance to the case and handled it very fairly. Each of the directors present believed that the company was already making substantial profits and there was no reason to increase prices, and unanimously opposed the proposal, and hence the proposal was not passed at that time. However, in case the company, unable to achieve its wish, resorts to other means against users, it is hoped that citizens will pay special attention. ㈠ The organizational charter of the French Municipal Council is still the temporary committee charter promulgated during the tenure of Consul-General Naziqi in 1926. It has been over seven years and still uses the temporary name without being revised, which is difficult to understand. Moreover, in recent years, the population of Chinese citizens has increased, and the tax amount has also increased year by year, but the number of Chinese directors has not been increased. Compared with the tax obligations fulfilled by Chinese citizens, the rights they should enjoy are very unequal. During the tenure of Consul-General Goring in 1931, after several negotiations, the appointed Chinese directors were changed to formally elected. However, when the list of Chinese directors elected this year was reported to the French Consulate-General for verification, the consulate replied that it would still use the old charter and appoint them, which deprives taxpayers of their right to elect representatives. It is urgent to request the French authorities to amend this temporary committee charter of the French Municipal Council as soon as possible, and increase the number of Chinese directors to comply with the principle of equal treatment between China and France. The association will then submit a request to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the French Minister. ㈠ The association has never had any regular funds. It should, in accordance with the precedent of the Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association, request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to forward a request to the Ministry of Finance to allocate funds. ㈠ The French Concession primary and secondary schools requested subsidies for educational expenses. Each Chinese director should propose to the Municipal Council to request appropriate subsidies and add Chinese children's primary schools to popularize Chinese education in the concession. The meeting adjourned at around 5 o'clock.

Last Year, National Customs Revenue Shortfall of 36 Million Taels

Shanghai Alone Reached 15 Million Taels, All Countries' Trade Affected by Japanese Militarism 119

Xinsheng News Agency, Nanjing. After the General Inspectorate of Customs reported the national customs revenue situation for the 21st year to Beijing, the authorities have not officially announced it. However, according to unofficial statements from the Ministry of Finance, the total national customs revenue last year was approximately 200 million Customs Taels, a decrease of approximately 36 million Taels compared to the total revenue of the previous year. Among them, Shanghai alone accounted for a decrease of as much as 15 million Taels. The remaining reductions were losses from the Northeast Customs and other ports. The losses in the Northeast were entirely due to the customs there being seized by the Japanese. The customs there had a small amount of revenue before March. The reason for the decrease in Shanghai was entirely due to the impact of the war. Although China's customs revenue decreased so much last year, it was still able to pay off domestic and foreign debts and indemnities on schedule without any delay. This also proves the Chinese government's credibility at home and abroad. The shortfall in tax revenue is certainly a direct loss to the Chinese government, but from this, it can also be seen to what extent the commerce of various countries in China has been affected by Japanese militarism.
