The Ministry of Finance Approves that Machine-Made Goods of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce are Still Exempt from Tax

Treated the Same as Native Goods 124

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously stated that imitation foreign soap, although reported to the regular customs after cutting the Likin tax, was not taxed. Now, goods that have been approved for machine-made treatment must be released after paying tax, which is really biased. It telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to order that they be exempted from tax together. The Ministry of Finance has now approved the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating that machine-made goods are still exempt from tax. The original text says: "The telegram has been noted. It has been found that regular customs in various places have been abolished. The regular customs mentioned in the telegram should refer to the Wusong Customs sub-card that has been re-established. In addition to ordering the General Inspectorate of Customs to investigate and reply, and verifying that machine-made goods transported domestically by sailboat or carriage that have not been taxed by the customs before, the customs should still exempt them from tax, so as to treat them the same as native goods to relieve manufacturers. This approval is for your information."

Two Railways Issue Round-Trip Tourist Tickets 125

In order to facilitate tourists traveling to Beijing and Hangzhou, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations plan to add two types of round-trip tourist tickets for the Beijing-Hangzhou first and second class special express trains. The Ministry of Railways has approved the plan. It is said that the ticket price will be 75% of the original round-trip price. The first class is 30.2 yuan, and the second class is 19.2 yuan. The validity period is set at ten days, and it can be divided into segments at the Shanghai North Station. It is said that the Railway Administration is rushing to print these tickets, which will be available for sale at the Beijing and Hangzhou stations from February 1st.

Recent Number of Japanese Residents in Shanghai

More Than 8,000 Fewer Than Before the War 126

Central News Agency reports that, according to Japanese sources, the number of Japanese residents in Shanghai was about 30,000 before the January 28th incident. During the war, it was only about 10,000. After the war stopped, Japanese residents came to Shanghai one after another. According to a recent survey, there are about 22,000 people. There are about 2,500 Japanese naval marines stationed in Shanghai, and about 100 Japanese police officers. As for the number of officers and men on Japanese warships, there is no definite number because they come and go frequently. The average number in Shanghai is about 500.

Citizens on Nanjing Road Sent a Letter to the Taxpayers Association Yesterday Opposing the Municipal Council's Increase in House Tax

Estimating High Rents Causes Social Unrest 128

The Nanjing Road Business Federation and the First District Branch of the Citizens Association, considering that the member stores Yiletian and Tongyuchun, etc., were forcibly assessed high rents and charged additional donations by the Municipal Council, sent a letter to the Taxpayers Association yesterday requesting it to forward the letter to the council to cancel the additional charges in order to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. The original letter said: "We are writing to you directly. The case of our member stores, Yiletian Teahouse at No. 513 Nanjing Road, and its affiliated Tongyuchun Teahouse at No. 463 Nanjing Road, received notices from the Municipal Council on December 23rd of last year, stating that Yiletian Teahouse, which pays 4,000 yuan in house tax annually, must be increased to 9,240 yuan per year from April 1st of this year. In addition, our affiliated Tongyuchun, which pays 4,400 yuan per year, must be increased to 6,240 yuan, which is more than one-half and one-third more than the original amount. However, after investigation, our company and affiliated company have been operating on Nanjing Road for more than ten years. As a rule, the donation is based on the original amount of the rent. Now the Municipal Council wants to forcibly estimate the price, treating the rent of old houses as the expensive rent of newly renovated houses, which is unfair. Moreover, our company's business is light and the profit is small, and it is barely maintained by using copper coins. Since 1928, the business has plummeted. If additional donations are added for no reason, it will be even more difficult to bear. We sincerely request your association to forward a letter to the Municipal Council to understand the merchants' difficulties and still collect donations according to the old amount, and also request the Citizens General Association and the Chinese Taxpayers Association to provide assistance together, etc. Upon approval, it has been found that the amount of house tax is based on the original amount of rent, which is an immutable principle. If the Municipal Council wants to increase revenue, it forcibly estimates high rents in order to charge additional donations, which is directly tyrannical and oppresses the people. It is heard that this is to encourage landlords to increase rents, and the underlying motive is to make the society increasingly unstable. This is a violation of the Municipal Council's duty to maintain public security. From the standpoint of taxpayers, not only is it difficult for stores whose business is barely maintained to bear the additional donations, but we also oppose the Municipal Council's move to estimate prices and collect donations. Even stores with flourishing businesses cannot recognize the tyrannical policy of estimating prices and collecting donations in the state of paying donations in accordance with the law. Approving the reason for the letter, we hereby request your association to forward a letter to the Municipal Council, stating that the house tax of Yiletian and Tongyuchun should always be collected according to the original amount, and stop similar administrative actions from being applied to any taxpayers, in order to maintain social stability and benefit the citizens' happy lives. To the extent of the public friendship, this is to the Chinese Taxpayers Association."

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Restructures Jianghai Shipping 132

Since Liu Hongsheng took over the reorganization of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, it has been several months. The internal organization has gradually been put in order. Now, they are starting to innovate and reorganize the business and ships. The reporter has investigated and reported the latest situation as follows:

Investigation of Yangtze River Freight Rates: The Yangtze River route is the main artery of the company's shipping business. Currently, the Jiang'an, Jiangxin, Jiangshun, Jianghua, Jiangda, Jiangjing, Jiangtian, Jianguo, Jiangyu, and Emei vessels operate. They are divided into two classes, A and B. For example, the Jiang'an, Jianghua, Jiangshun, and Jiangbei vessels are Class A ships, running on Mondays and Thursdays. The other vessels run on Tuesdays and Fridays. If the company can effectively reorganize the Yangtze River business, it can compete with Butterfield & Swire and Jardine Matheson. President Liu has started by focusing on the Yangtze River. He has discussed with the Head of the Business Department, He Molin, and the Head of the Shipping Department, Zhao Yuntai, and others to standardize the Yangtze River freight rates to gain the trust of customers.

The two departments of business and shipping have been specially ordered to send commissioners to organize a water freight investigation committee to thoroughly investigate the actual situation in various ports upstream and downstream in order to verify and set standard freight rates.

Request to Build Steamers and Tugs: On the Yangtze River route, Butterfield & Swire, Jardine Matheson, and others have selected and replaced new ships in recent years, but the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company still uses old ships. Some of the older ships are over 30 years old, with low speed and high coal consumption. The productivity is minimal, and the cost is twice that of foreign ships, which is not cost-effective. Therefore, Zhao Yuntai, the Head of the Shipping Department, has specially requested President Liu to continue to add new Yangtze River steamers under 3,000 tons, four Yangtze River steamers of 1,000 tons, two upper Yangtze River steamers of 500 tons, and 15 iron barges and self-propelled barges to be distributed within the Yangtze River to meet the needs. Moreover, it is stipulated that the old Yangtze River steamers will be allocated to government-rented transport ships. The Class A ships can only be used for commercial purposes and cannot be transferred for use to avoid delays and cause distrust among customers.

South China Stipulates Schedules: Last year, the entire fleet of ships was affected by the current situation, but the South China shipping routes flourished instead. For example, Butterfield & Swire, Jardine Matheson, and other companies lost money on all routes last year, but the Shantou-Xiamen-Hong Kong lines of the South China route were fully loaded each time and made huge profits. The South China shipping routes of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company have always been the fundamental routes for coastal shipping. In recent years, since the accidents of Xinhua and Xinchang, there has not been a single ship that meets the regulations for sailing to Hong Kong. Although there is one ship, Gongping, it can only carry cargo and cannot transport passengers to Hong Kong. Now, the Shipping Department plans to first request the company to lease three ocean-going ships to operate in South China to develop business and restore the long-suspended Hong Kong liner. At the same time, they will request to build three new ocean-going ships of 3,000 tons to allow the South China line to have six ships operating, with the Shantou-Hong Kong-Guangdong line running on Mondays, Wednesdays, and Fridays, and the Xiamen-Hong Kong-Guangdong line running on Tuesdays, Thursdays, and Saturdays, in order to gradually compete and recover the freight lost to foreign ships.

Xu Etang, Manager of Tian Qing Xiang, Commits Suicide

Commits Suicide by Poison Due to Poor Business, Leaving a Will to Purchase a Coffin and Clothes with 50 Gold Pieces 133

Xu Etang, also known as Tang, a 54-year-old Ningbo native and manager of Da Qing Xiang Leather Goods Store at 384 Henan Road, Public Concession, was known for his shrewd planning and capable work. He had been working at the store for six years and had annual surpluses, which the store owner greatly valued. Since the impact of the January 28 Incident last year, the leather business has plummeted, and inventory is piling up like mountains while new goods continue to arrive to maintain appearances. Recently, with the Lunar New Year approaching, finances have become tight, and turnover is difficult. Various accounts cannot be paid. Xu, with his upright nature, felt ashamed to ask the store owner for funds due to the poor business and huge expenses. In a moment of anger, he considered suicide. He went out around 4:00 PM the day before and returned to the store around 7:00 PM in the evening, having purchased strong opium. After dinner, he went upstairs to bed. At around 9:00 AM yesterday, he had not yet gotten up. His son entered the room to check on him and saw him lying stiffly on the bed, barely alive. He found an opium box and realized that he had committed suicide by taking poison. He was immediately taken to Renji Hospital for treatment, but due to the severe poisoning, he could not be saved and died shortly after. Beforehand, he had written a will, with the envelope addressed to Xu Etang's message, stating that purchasing a medium-quality coffin and clothes would cost 50 yuan, which would be enough. He also wrote that he was too ashamed to face anyone due to his sudden death, in a few words of extreme sorrow. According to various investigations by reporters, Xu's suicide was only due to a shortage of over 10,000 gold pieces, which is also pitiful.

(5) Committee Member Wang Qizhang's letter inquiring about the number of people required to form a medical association according to the draft proposal submitted in accordance with proposals 33 and 41 of the general assembly. (Resolution) The number of people required to form a medical association will be based on the second article of the Shanghai Medical Association's previous draft opinions on the Ministry of Health's regulations for medical associations (original text: the number of doctors should be at least ten or more, which is certainly appropriate, but considering that there are very few doctors nationwide, it is easy for each city and county to reach five people, but in order to establish medical associations, it seems necessary to temporarily reduce the basic number of people to five).

City Health Bureau Stipulates Two Regulations

Revised Regulations for the Management of Food and Beverage Establishments 137

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, recognizing the increasing number of food and beverage establishments in the city, has deemed it necessary to revise the previously established regulations for the management of such establishments, as well as the regulations pertaining to food and beverage production and premises, to better align with the current situation. The original twenty-nine articles have been consolidated into twenty-two, and submitted to the municipal government for approval and implementation. The revised regulations are appended below: (Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau Regulations for the Management of Food and Beverage Establishments), Revised October 19, 1932. Chapter I: General Provisions. Article 1: All restaurants, wine shops, caterers, pastry shops, snack shops, noodle shops, bakeries, dim sum shops, hotels, tea houses, and other establishments that sell food and beverages for immediate consumption shall be considered within the scope of these regulations. Article 2: Any individual wishing to open a food or beverage establishment must first report to the Bureau by filling out a form. The Bureau will investigate to ensure that there are no health hazards or that improvements have been made accordingly. Upon confirmation, a business permit will be issued. A fee of one silver dollar will be charged for each permit, and it must be renewed annually. Article 3: Food and beverage establishments shall be subject to the guidance of the Bureau and shall diligently implement improvements in hygiene at all times. Chapter II: Equipment. Article 4: Walls should be kept clean, and the roof and walls should be thoroughly cleaned at least twice a year, with whitewashing done in both summer and winter. Kitchens and food preparation areas should be washed daily and kept free of accumulated dirt. Lavatories should not be located adjacent to kitchens, food preparation areas, or dining areas, and should be frequently cleaned and disinfected with disinfectant or lime water to prevent foul odors. Article 5: Sufficient spittoons containing disinfectant or lime water should be provided. Spitting, littering, and discarding refuse are prohibited. Covered garbage cans should be provided for temporary storage, and emptied daily. Indiscriminate dumping is prohibited. Article 6: Cups, plates, bowls, chopsticks, and utensils used for storing food and beverages, as well as guest towels, should be washed and disinfected with boiling water after each use before being used again. Article 7: Ingredients that easily attract flies should be covered with gauze. Ingredients that are easily perishable should be stored in refrigerators. Unhygienic and leftover items must not be used as ingredients. Food and beverage items should be stored in appropriate containers to prevent dust, flies, and mosquitoes from contaminating them. Chapter III: Employees. Article 8: All manufacturers and servers in food and beverage establishments must be vaccinated against smallpox and cholera, typhoid fever by the Bureau and shall follow instructions to prevent various infectious diseases. If anyone suffers from tuberculosis, dysentery, typhoid fever, skin or venereal diseases, or other infectious diseases, regardless of the severity, they must be temporarily suspended from work and may not return to work until they obtain a certificate of full recovery from a public Shanghai hospital designated by the Bureau. Employees or employers who are temporarily suspended from work due to infectious diseases shall be treated in accordance with industry regulations or customary practices. Article 9: Employees shall request a medical examination from a public Shanghai hospital designated by the Bureau once a year. If there are no infectious diseases, the hospital will issue a certificate. This certificate shall be presented when renewing the permit each year in order to be granted the permit (the hospital will only charge a paper fee of two silver cents for this certificate each time). Article 10: Employees should bathe, have haircuts, and change clothes frequently to maintain cleanliness and a neat appearance. They should also wear clean aprons while serving. Article 11: Employees shall earnestly maintain cleanliness in the shop under the direction of the owner, manager, or foreman. Chapter IV: Penalties. Article 12: Those who violate the provisions of Article 2 of these regulations shall be fined between two and fifteen yuan. Article 13: Those who violate the provisions of Article 3 of these regulations and refuse to make improvements after being instructed to do so shall be fined between five and fifteen yuan by the manager or owner of the shop. Article 14: Those who violate the provisions of each article in Chapter II of these regulations shall be fined between five jiao and fifteen yuan depending on the circumstances. Article 15: If a food and beverage establishment has been penalized twice and is found to have violated the regulations again within six months, and still refuses to make improvements after being instructed to do so by the Bureau, it shall be fined between fifteen and fifty yuan and may be ordered to suspend operations. Article 16: Those who violate the provisions of Article 8 of these regulations shall be fined between one and fifteen yuan by the shop manager or owner. Article 17: Those who violate the provisions of Articles 9, 10, and 11 of these regulations shall be fined between five jiao and one yuan per employee, to be paid by the shop. Article 18: Fines shall be paid by the penalized party to the Bureau, and an official receipt will be issued immediately. If anyone comes to the shop to collect fines without an official receipt, it is a case of impersonation and extortion. The penalized party may report the facts for investigation and prosecution. Article 19: Shop owners shall strictly comply with these regulations and shall not offer bribes or monthly fees to inspectors or police officers. Once verified, both the giver and receiver of the bribe will be sent to the court for strict punishment according to the law. Chapter V: Supplementary Provisions. Article 20: The executing agencies for the various items stipulated in these regulations are the Bureau or the Shanghai Municipal Police Department or the affiliated districts. Receipts for fines shall be stamped with the official seal of the Bureau or the Police Department to ensure authenticity. Article 21: These regulations may be revised at any time if there are any matters not covered. Article 22: These regulations shall be implemented upon approval and promulgation by the Shanghai Municipal Government. (Note) Food and beverage establishments in Zou Village (and all towns and markets in the thirteen districts of Wusong, Yinhang, Jiangwan, Pengpu, Zhenru, Pusong, Fahua, Caojing, Tangqiao, Yangsi, Luhang, Gaohang, and Gaoqiao) are granted a reduction of half the permit fee (fifty cents) for opening a business, according to Instruction No. 3305 issued by the Municipal Government on December 2, 1929.

Provisional Regulations for the Management of Food and Beverage Manufacturing Plants by the Bureau of Health and the Bureau of Social Affairs 138

1. All establishments in this city that are open for the manufacture of food and beverages should abide by these regulations to emphasize hygiene.

2. All manufacturers of food and beverages are required to pay a fee of one yuan to petition the Bureau of Health for inspection. Upon approval, they shall receive a joint license from the Bureau of Health and the Bureau of Social Affairs. This license must be renewed annually.

3. This license may not be transferred to others and must be displayed in a prominent location within the manufacturing plant.

4. Any manufacturing plant with an attached retail department shall comply with the regulations for the management of food and beverage establishments in this city.

5. The construction, installation, and repair of factory buildings must be reported in advance and carried out in accordance with the instructions of both Bureaus. They shall also comply with the instructions of both Bureaus at any time to modify or add to the buildings to make them suitable.

6. Spitting is prohibited in all areas of the plant. The surroundings of the plant must be kept clean. The workshop and food storage areas must not be used for sleeping or gathering for meals and must be equipped with fly-prevention facilities.

7. The plant must have clean toilets and screened windows. Bathrooms must be provided where necessary.

8. Every year in April and October of the solar calendar, all buildings should be thoroughly cleaned and refreshed.

9. The employment or accommodation of persons suffering from infectious or skin diseases is prohibited. The Bureau of Health must be notified immediately of any illnesses or deaths. All employees in the plant must be vaccinated against smallpox and cholera, typhoid fever by the Bureau of Health and must comply with instructions to prevent various infectious diseases.

10. The manufacture of food is not permitted to be adulterated, misrepresented, or to use toxic pigments or unsanitary raw materials. When manufacturing, attention should be paid to cleanliness. It is not permissible to use unclean water to mix raw materials and it is not permissible to spray any liquid on food by mouth.

11. All foods sent for sale, such as bread, must be wrapped and stored in paper or other clean items to prevent contamination by dust, flies, etc.

12. The wrappers of bread and the cans and glass bottles of biscuits, sweets, soda water, beer, and other food and beverage items must be approved by both Bureaus and bear the printed name, address of the manufacturing plant, and the exact weight or capacity of the food.

13. All those delivering food and beverages must carry a delivery voucher with the joint seal of both Bureaus for the current year. If such a delivery voucher is lost, it must be reported to both Bureaus and a fee of one yuan paid to obtain a new voucher.

14. All baskets used for delivering food and beverages must be cleaned and tightly covered, and must not contain clothes, bedding, or other unclean items. The name and address of the manufacturing plant must be clearly marked on the baskets and utensils.

15. All manufacturing plants must allow inspectors from the Bureau of Health and the Bureau of Social Affairs, who are wearing staff identification, to enter and inspect, but must not offer bribes or gifts.

16. The Bureau of Health may, when it deems necessary, take samples for testing, but must provide a receipt. If the test reveals inferior products or unsanitary substances, or that they are not suitable for consumption, they will be penalized.

17. Violators of these regulations shall be fined up to five yuan depending on the circumstances. Repeat offenders may be fined between five and twenty-five yuan and have their licenses revoked.

18. These regulations shall be promulgated and implemented upon approval by the Municipal Government.

Cook Imprisons Himself as Host Out of Curiosity and is Kidnapped 140

The Host Receives an Intimidation Letter and Ignores It

The Cook Goes to the Appointment to Investigate

Three Kidnappers Actually Take Him Away

The Orderly Urgently Returns Home to Report

Feng Guoying, styled Songqing, is a native of Fujian, 43 years old, residing at 21 Rue Sainte Marie, French Concession. He formerly served as the section chief of the second section of the Military Commission's Management Department of the National Government. He recently retired last month. At about 3:00 PM yesterday, when Feng was about to take a car to Nanjing, he suddenly received an anonymous letter stating that due to extreme financial need, Feng was being asked to pay a ransom of 50,000 yuan, limited to 8:00 PM last night at the Oriental Hotel bookstore at the intersection of Xizang Road and Guangdong Road. It was also specified that the money should be handed over to someone in the bookstore wearing a suit and holding a bundle of newspapers. Feng simply laughed it off at the time and set off with his luggage. Unexpectedly, Feng's cook, Liu Yinquan (25 years old) from Henan, found out about the matter. Liu, being very curious, privately agreed with Feng's orderly to go with him at the appointed time. After arriving at the entrance of the Oriental Hotel, Liu instructed the orderly to watch from across the street. He then went straight into the bookstore. He saw two people wearing suits, one holding a bundle of newspapers, and one wearing a long gown waiting at the entrance of the bookstore. Liu immediately went forward to speak with them. Unexpectedly, when these three people saw that Liu did not mention the ransom, they immediately grabbed Liu and took him out of the Oriental Hotel, pushed him into a car at the entrance, and drove away quickly. At that time, the orderly who was waiting across the street saw Liu being kidnapped into the car and, knowing that it was difficult to call for help, frantically ran back home to report. After deliberation by Feng's wife and Feng's younger brother, they urgently reported the matter to the police station for investigation. The police station immediately dispatched a large number of detectives to search around the clock. It is reported that there are already clues.

The Shanghai YWCA has always been very willing to do its best for patriotic mutual assistance and obligations. Now, upon learning of the plight of refugees in the Yuguan area, who are suffering from the cold without food or clothing, and are displaced, the Association is deeply saddened and ashamed that it is unable to help them. Recently, they received a telegram from the Beijing YWCA asking them to donate money and clothing to be forwarded to the local relief efforts. The Association is urgently conducting a donation drive. In addition to starting with members of the Association, it is hoped that patriotic ladies will voluntarily contribute and send donations to the new premises of the Association at 8 Yuanmingyuan Road, C, 3rd Floor (telephone 13322). At this time of national crisis, it is believed that there are still many people who sympathize with the Association. For this kind of public service that is easy to accomplish, everyone will certainly do their best.

The Chen Tugen Case Opens 144

The case of Ling Jiannan, a native of Chuansha, who was killed by expelled detective Wang Wencai and others in Ximen Ningkang Lane, was heard yesterday by Judge Qian of the District Court. Chen Tugen, who had been in custody, was brought to court. Chen Tugen was a fugitive from the detention center who had been recaptured. Judge Qian immediately interrogated Chen Tugen about the circumstances of Ling Jiannan's death. However, Chen Tugen stubbornly denied everything. The Judge then asked Chen if he knew Wang Daxin and Huang Zicheng, etc. Chen replied that he did not know them. The Judge then asked Huang Zicheng. Huang claimed that he did not hide Wang Wencai, etc., and that he did not know them either. As for the first summons from the court, the name on the summons was Wang Datian, but my name is Huang Zicheng, so I wrote a name on the bailiff's statement and could not appear in court. The second summons corrected the name, and I went to Hankou. Because I wrote my own name, they knew that I was Huang Zicheng, so I was falsely accused. Huang Shaoying testified that he did not know how Wang Wencai, etc., went to kill people, and that he was not at home. The court also summoned the police officer on duty that day to testify that after Ling Jiannan was injured, his wife shouted to catch the thief, and I apprehended Chen Tugen. Chen said that he was not a thief, but was in a fight. At that time, Chen had no weapon in his hand, and I did not see Huang Zicheng and Huang Shaoying. The Judge, considering that the case still required further investigation, ordered Chen Tugen to be detained and the others to return home to await instructions.

Japanese Lieutenant Commander Fukuda's Naval Funeral Held Yesterday

Warships Fly Half-Mast, Land Forces Fire Salutes 147

Japanese Navy Third Fleet Staff Officer Lieutenant Commander Fukuda Isamu, a strong proponent of Sino-Japanese friendship, died of acute pneumonia while serving in Shanghai. At 2:00 PM yesterday, Commander Minai of the Third Fleet held a naval funeral ceremony for Fukuda's body. Chief of Staff Kikuno of the same fleet was appointed as the director of the sea burial, with staff officer Okuma, Marine Corps staff officer Sakai, naval attaché Kobetto, and Marine Corps chief of staff Kawamura as committee members. Minai ordered all officers of all ranks from the Izumo, Tenryu, Hishi, Ashi, and Tung warships stationed in Shanghai to participate, and dispatched a company of marines, a military band, a company of military police, and a squad of Japanese police from the consulate to gather in front of the Zhaizhang set up at the Hongkou Marine Corps headquarters. When each representative went to pay respects, a small cannon was fired 120 times. At 2:15 PM, the procession escorted Fukuda's coffin to the cemetery for burial. The entire honor guard of the Izumo warship participated. Minai also ordered all Japanese warships in Shanghai to fly half-mast in mourning. On the Chinese side, Tang Mang, Wang Qingchen, Chen Zemin, and others all went to express their condolences. Xiao Baixin even offered condolences with the lines "His noble spirit filled the heavens, his great ambitions were not fulfilled, the general star fell on the sea, and tears flowed on the guest journey." Fukuda had served in China as the captain of the Yangtze River gunboats Sumida and Atami for a long time and was a strong advocate of Sino-Japanese friendship.

Freight Forwarding and Customs Declaration Industry Hosts Banquet for Customs Officials

Tax Affairs Director's Understanding of Merchants' Difficulties 148

The Shanghai City Forwarding and Customs Clearance Association, representing all its members, has been facing immense difficulties since the Jianghai Customs implemented its new regulations last year. The regulations require members to pay exorbitant security deposits and impose various harsh treatments, making it practically unbearable for the customs clearance industry. The association had previously submitted a petition to the Director-General of Customs and the Finance and Customs Affairs Department, requesting the cancellation of the new regulations to alleviate the merchants' plight. However, the outcome was nearly zero, and the Customs continued its severe penalties. Consequently, the Chairman of the Association, Shi Zhikun, You Senting, and others, specially sought the assistance of shipping magnates to explain their hardships in detail to Director Luo.

Director Luo showed understanding. Last night, at 6:30 PM, the association held a Western-style banquet on the fourth floor of the Shipping Club at 10 Guangdong Road. Guests included Director Luo, Customs Directors Ford and others, as well as shipping leaders Liu Hongsheng (China Merchants), Yu Qiaqing (Sanbei), Yang Nanmei (Butterfield & Swire), Jardine Matheson representatives Lawyer, George White, Tate, Lin Yongxiang (Jardine), Yuan Ludeng (Ning Shao). The customs clearance industry's Chairman Shi Zhikun, Zhou Jingzhai, You Senting, and Zheng Renye warmly welcomed the guests. Halfway through the banquet, Chairman Shi Zhikun rose to deliver a speech, briefly stating that the past misunderstandings between the Customs and the industry had now been resolved through Director Luo's understanding. Regarding the security deposit required by the new regulations, the association had already raised 100,000 yuan to deposit in the Central Bank as the industry's security deposit. Director Luo was also well aware that the customs clearance industry was not without assets. As for the various harsh penalties imposed by the Customs, Director Luo had agreed to consider them. However, he mentioned the complexity of the industry's members and the frequent disturbances caused at the Customs, hoping for rectification. It had been decided with Director Luo that in the future, Customs would give priority to customs brokerage firms joining the association, and sternly eliminate and eradicate unlicensed brokers. He earnestly hoped that the staff and apprentices sent by the industry to the Customs would strictly abide by Customs regulations to maintain their personal integrity and status. Director Luo also rose to give a brief response, stating that he was very pleased to gather for dinner and that it was not appropriate to discuss official matters. However, the various difficulties of the customs clearance industry had been fully understood after Chairman Shi's statement, and the treatment of the industry would certainly be improved in the future. The banquet then concluded.

Tea and Snack Workers of Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Petitioned Party and Government Organs Yesterday

Also Telegraphing the People's Movement Association and the Ministry of Railways Requesting Cessation of Bureau's Bidding 151

Due to the Railway Bureau's bidding for the tea and snack services, causing panic among the tea and snack workers of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, they sent representatives to petition the two Bureau Directors, Huang Boqiao, the day before yesterday, but without result. Therefore, at 10 AM yesterday morning, they dispatched representatives to petition the Municipal Government with a written statement. Secretary Wang Shaozhai received them and stated that since the matter concerned labor-capital disputes, he would transfer it to the Social Affairs Bureau for handling according to the law. They then proceeded to petition the Municipal Party Department, where the Chief Director of the People's Training Section, Zhang Sheng, received them and promised to submit a request for approval. The workers issued a declaration yesterday and telegraphed the Central People's Training Association and the Ministry of Railways, requesting the cessation of the Bureau's bidding, and planned to send representatives to Nanjing and Beijing. The original telegram and declaration are recorded below.

Telegraph: Nanjing Central People's Movement Guidance Committee, Railways Ministry, esteemed sirs. This time, the Bureau suddenly, during the effective period of the renewed contract for the tea and snack services on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, rashly posted a public tender for contracting, causing extremely serious repercussions. Evidence was collected and mailed on the removed date, requesting investigation and handling. Despite repeated petitions, the Party Department of the Bureau has shown no signs of assistance. However, the Bureau has decided to implement the bidding on removed date, and the lives of hundreds of workers will inevitably be sacrificed as a result. The bidding period is secret, the situation is tense, and an unprecedented catastrophe is imminent. We urgently request an immediate telegram to the Bureau to stop the bidding. To avoid expansion, this is the only way. Anxious and urgent telegram, awaiting orders. The Shanghai-Hangzhou Section Tea and Snack Workers Anti-Subcontracting Movement Executive Committee, General Director Sun Wenpin, Deputy General Directors Zhou Panlin, Lu Yisheng, jointly kowtow.

Declaration: Investigation reveals that the Bureau uses the subcontracting system to oppress workers, and the most prominent in this harmful relationship are the subcontractors of tea, snacks, catering, and loading/unloading, who apply their oppressive tactics to the greatest extent. The events of the past make us believe it even more. However, the rise and fall of the subcontracting system are closely related to the vital interests of the workers. At this time of thoroughly eradicating the subcontracting trend, there is indeed a dilemma. Therefore, the workers of tea, snacks, catering, loading, and unloading groups recognize this as a matter of life and death, and it is essential to abolish subcontracting and operate independently. Thus, they rose one after another to launch the anti-subcontracting movement, finally achieving the goal of the Bureau abolishing subcontractors and the workers directly undertaking the services. Proof of this can be found in August of the 17th year of the Republic, when the Bureau revoked the contract signed with subcontractor Yao Xigeng for the Jing-Hu dining car service and returned it to the workers to undertake. At that time, the Shanghai-Hangzhou tea and snack workers were still under the control of subcontractor Xu Huisheng, enduring unbearable oppression. They launched another anti-subcontracting movement, and finally, in May of the 18th year of the Republic, representatives were commissioned by various higher-level organizations to supervise the signing of labor-capital reconciliation conditions, guaranteeing that the workers would no longer be subjected to subcontractor oppression. When the subcontractor's contract expired, the Bureau would grant the tea and snack workers the priority right to undertake the services directly. This was the main regulation for resolving the dispute. Therefore, in July of the 10th year of the Republic, the Bureau, based on the priority right, signed the first direct contract with the workers to undertake the tea and snack services, for a term of one year. The second renewal of the new contract was also officially signed by both parties on September 19th of the 21st year of the Republic, and the security deposit was fully paid, with complete procedures and a solid foundation. Even if the contract expired, it should still be renewed according to precedent. However, during the legally effective period, not only was the new contract withheld and not issued, becoming ironclad evidence of intentional breach of faith, but also a public tender was announced, further revealing the contradiction of their behavior, using the deceitful tactic of deceiving themselves to destroy legal rights. How should we emphasize the importance of maintaining the livelihood of the workers? Would we rather restore subcontracting and allow them to poison the people? The absurdity of reason has reached this extreme. Our Association is determined to unite and resist insults, driven by justice to fight, grieving over the fickleness, expressing a solemn public opinion, and vowing not to give up until the bidding is abolished. We respectfully hope that enthusiastic organizations at home and abroad will rise up to support us, so that justice can triumph over power. We beg the attention of all sectors. This declaration is respectfully submitted for your consideration. Shanghai-Hangzhou Section Tea and Snack Workers Anti-Subcontracting Movement Executive Committee respectfully.

A Difficult Situation for the Lawyer's Secretary in a Smuggling Case Where the Bail Money is Confiscated 152

Zheng Qiaji's tobacco firm, for the sake of providing excellent service to its customers, would dispatch employees to deliver opium for purchases exceeding ten taels, in order to avoid any danger during transit. Xu Genlin and his wife, Wang, served as delivery personnel for several years, without any previous incidents. Unexpectedly, in November, Mr. Xu was transporting a large quantity of opium in a rented car to a location in the International Settlement, when he was apprehended and the opium confiscated. He was handed over to the First Special District Court for interrogation and punishment. His lawyer, Zhang Zongding, filed an appeal, and he was granted bail after posting a 2,000 yuan bond, pending further review. When the appellate court summoned him for questioning, Mr. and Mrs. Xu repeatedly failed to appear. Consequently, the appellate court rejected the appeal and ordered the confiscation of the 2,000 yuan bond. However, Mr. and Mrs. Xu did not realize that trafficking opium was illegal and punishable by law. Instead, they blamed their lawyer, Zhang Chongding, for ineffective defense. They went to Mr. Zhang's office, and, as he was unavailable, they tricked Mr. Zhang's secretary, Cheng Xinglin, into going to the Xu residence in the French Concession, claiming that Mr. Zhang had to compensate them for the confiscated 2,000 yuan bond and return the lawyer's fee before they would release him. After repeated negotiations between the parties, Cheng Xinglin finally regained his freedom. However, Cheng felt deeply humiliated by this ordeal, as he was not involved in the matter. Therefore, he argued with the Xus for a long time, but to no avail. Cheng has now filed a criminal complaint with the First Special District Court against Xu Wang, Xu Genlin's wife, for restricting his freedom. Since being released on bail in the opium case, she has evaded capture. Regarding Cheng's complaint,

she has also repeatedly failed to appear in court, and Judge Shen Bingrong continued the hearing yesterday morning. However, as the defendant Xu Wang was still unable to be summoned, the trial could not proceed and was adjourned to a later date.

The Dashing Thief in the Customs 153

| Confesses to the Ingenious Method of Pawning Typewriters |

In recent months, repeated thefts have occurred in the Jianghai Customs' main writing room and second-floor appraisal room. Numerous items of clothing, such as coats, fur robes, camel hair robes, and mandarin jackets, have been stolen. On the 19th and 28th of last month, two typewriters, one large and one small, were stolen from the appraisal room. The total losses amount to over a thousand yuan. The greatest victim was clerk Shi Cunqiao. The thief's usual attire was very dashing, and he moved in and out of the Customs freely, causing others not to pay attention to him. Unexpectedly, the thief went to the Customs again the day before yesterday to carry out his old trick, and was noticed and captured by clerk Shi. The Water Police Station was notified, and detectives Wu Rongsheng and Su Jinlong were dispatched to take the suspect back to the police station. Under interrogation, the suspect confessed his name was Lin Aquan, 23 years old, from Qingpu, without a fixed occupation, specializing in theft to make a living. He also said that his accomplices included Zhang Atao and others. When the police asked if he had committed thefts elsewhere, Lin confessed to stealing a typewriter from the window of the China and Foreign Telephone Company. He also stated that pawning a typewriter required a guarantor, so he came up with a method: he falsely claimed to the pawnshop that it was being pawned from a certain foreign barracks, and instructed the pawnshop clerk to accompany him to the gate of a certain foreign barracks. He first had the pawnshop clerk wait outside, and then he went inside to falsely claim he was looking for a friend, circled around, and came out again. He had previously written some Western characters with a black pen on a piece of foreign paper, which he gave to the clerk to take back as proof. Therefore, the pawnshop believed him and was willing to accept the pawn. After verifying his confession, the police dispatched detectives to the pawnshops he mentioned and redeemed a夹大衣, a camel hair robe, and three typewriters, which were returned to the victims. Yesterday, the police took the suspect to the Public Concession Police Station for further interrogation. It was discovered that he had also committed numerous other crimes. He was then taken back to the Water Police Station and detained pending transfer to the court for trial.

Liu Guobao and Li Shiying Sentenced to Death 154

Wang Bin, a detective from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, was assassinated by communist enemies on the afternoon of April 23rd of last year while riding in a rented car on Avenue Vilmont in the French Concession. His driver also suffered the same fate. Less than a month later, Cao Qingcheng, a Hubei native and inspector of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, who lived in Yuancheng Lane on Avenue Lafayette, was also assassinated on Avenue Kelle, and Jin Shoupei, a native of Jiangwan, was mistakenly killed because of mistaken identity. Detectives pursued the suspects to locations such as Rue Bayle, where they apprehended the murderers Liu Guobao, a Sichuan native (17 years old), and Li Shiying, a Henan native. They confiscated handguns. Later, they went to the residence of Liu and Li at 305 Weihaiwei Road and arrested another accomplice, Li Zecai from Anhui. They also went to 980 Huade Road and arrested suspect Zhu Jinming and others, confiscating handguns, bullets, bayonets, handcuffs, and other items. They were sent to the Jiangsu High Court Third Branch for prosecution. The case has been heard and is awaiting judgment, as reported previously. Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, the police brought the defendants to court. The Criminal Court sentenced Liu Guobao and Li Shiying to ten years imprisonment each for forming an organization with the purpose of endangering the Republic of China and depriving them of their civil rights for fifteen years. They were each sentenced to death for premeditated murder and deprived of their civil rights for life. The death sentences will be carried out. Li Zecai was sentenced to ten years imprisonment for forming an organization with the purpose of endangering the Republic of China and deprived of his civil rights for fifteen years. He was sentenced to ten years imprisonment for conspiracy to commit murder and deprived of his civil rights for fifteen years. He will serve a total of nineteen years imprisonment and be deprived of his civil rights for fifteen years. The number of days of detention will be deducted from the prison sentence. Four handguns, 681 bullets, 19 bullet magazines, 4 bayonets, and 2 handcuffs will be confiscated. Liu Guobao, Li Shiying, and Li Zecai were found not guilty of the other charges against them. Zhu Jinming was found not guilty. After the judgment was read, the court explained the reasons for the judgment to each defendant. Liu and the two Lis were taken back into custody. Zhu Jinming had submitted a petition requesting bail, which the court granted upon finding a suitable guarantor for 1,000 yuan pending review. However, in this case, there was no evidence in the investigation regarding the murder of Wang Bin, so no conviction was made on that charge.

Reader Consultant

Can Personality Be Exchanged for Food? 166

丨Letter from Mr. Weng Chongshi丨

(Since Mr. Weng's first letter was published in this column on December 19th, Mr. Zhu Yingsun and Mr. Jingren have subsequently written, repeatedly discussing our reply. 丨See this column on December 19th, 22nd, 27th, and 31st丨 We have now received a follow-up letter from Mr. Weng, which we are publishing below, followed by our reply.)

The people demanding debts have been coming incessantly, all with cold and sarcastic remarks. My wife is narrow-minded and cannot bear such humiliation, so she is constantly complaining to me. She says things like, "A person cannot get rich without unexpected wealth!" and "Many students are selling Japanese goods and smuggling opium, and they are living so happily now! You insist on adhering to the three prohibitions (prostitution, gambling, and drinking) and on maintaining your personality. Now you are suffering like this! Can personality be exchanged for food?" Alas! Sir, is what my wife says correct? Indeed, many people were so enthusiastically patriotic when they were students, but why do they all change completely once they enter society and start working?

In this cold and indifferent world, besides you, the reporter, I didn't think there were still Mr. Zhu Ying and Mr. Sun Jingren who sympathize with me. I am truly grateful! I beg you to tell me their addresses! Also, on January 1st, in your reply to Mr. Sun Jingren, you said, "We further hope that everyone can have a thorough awakening..." The meaning of the word "awakening" is quite vague. Please explain the "steps" of awakening as much as possible!

Reply: Reading your letter naturally fills us with endless indignation! Your wife's words are extremely painful! Of course, everyone knows that what she said is wrong, but no one can produce facts to refute it. However, I must ask, can this current state of affairs continue? We want to tell your wife that this will certainly not last long! Our society is now falling into a deep abyss of decline. No wonder everything around us is pitch black. And some people who will soon "die peacefully in their beds" seem to feel that their heaven is experiencing violent tremors. At the same time, they do not understand what kind of world will exist after these violent tremors. In their minds, perhaps it will still be theirs. Therefore, enjoyment and indulgence dominate everything they do. In this brief moment, they doubly expose their "ugliness" and fully unleash their "beastly desires," wasting their last bit of destiny! To put it kindly, this is "a final burst of glory before death"; to put it badly, it is "hastening death"! Your wife only sees their enjoyment and not their dark side. She thinks they are still in heaven, but in fact, they will soon be "buried." This momentary enjoyment is merely the prelude to their death knell! Here, we must ask ourselves: are we willing to follow them into the grave? Or are we going to find our own path to light and create our own paradise? If you are willing to crawl into the grave with them, then by all means pursue momentary, shallow pleasures. Otherwise, we should endure our hardships! Poverty is not the end of everything—we believe that the word "poverty" will soon disappear from the dictionary. If a person is afraid of poverty, then he is finished. Of course, we must eat, but "wanting to eat" is definitely not the same as "being afraid of poverty." We must distinguish this clearly. Now, on the one hand, we must strive to develop "light," and on the other hand, we must push this "cold and indifferent world" to accelerate its destruction. This work may be arduous, but because it is arduous, we should make redoubled efforts! I hope that you and your wife can both understand this clearly. You also asked: what are the steps for awakening? Please reread my reply to Mr. Sun's original letter. It says: "Ask why most people suffer and cannot get enough to eat, or want to suffer but have no suffering to endure? Why do a few people not suffer at all and attain 'peace, wealth, and honor'?" If you can answer these questions, then you are awakened. There do not need to be any "steps" in this. As long as you can understand the origins of your "suffering," that is enough. As for how to deal with the incessant debt collectors, we have already said in our previous letter: repay if you can; if you can't, let them do what they want. If you simply ignore them, what can they do? Of course, if they can forgive your difficulties and discuss solutions with you politely, you should welcome that. Otherwise, you absolutely do not need to be afraid of them! You must also relax a little and absolutely do not worry. Even if you worry a lot, none of the debt collectors will forgive you.

(Mr. Weng hopes that we will tell him the contact addresses of Mr. Zhu Ying and Mr. Sun Jingren. Unfortunately, we do not even know the contact addresses of these two gentlemen. Here, we will introduce Mr. Weng to Mr. Zhu and Mr. Sun. Mr. Weng is currently the principal of the First Central Elementary School in Fuqing City, Fujian. If you two would like to correspond with him, please write directly to him. If you are willing to tell us your contact addresses, we would also be very happy.)

Important Educational News

Universities in Beiping Release Students Early for Winter Vacation 167

丨Zhu Jia骅 Expresses His Opinion丨

Only One Day Away from the Scheduled Winter Vacation

Therefore, There is No Need to Issue Another Order to Prevent It

(Nanjing 17th, Telegram) Zhu Jia骅 said that the Ministry of Education believes that universities in Beiping released students early for winter vacation because the national crisis is becoming increasingly urgent, and it is a time for young people to bury themselves in their studies.

Since it is only one day away from the scheduled winter vacation for universities on January 18th, there is no need to issue another order to prevent it. As for the citizens of Beiping who requested that the government allocate the educational funds for universities in Beiping during the suspension of classes to the anti-Japanese cause, the Ministry of Education has not yet received this request and has no opinion to express. However, university funding is determined by the government and should not be diverted casually, he said.

Ministry of Education Discusses Elementary School Regulations 168

丨To be Announced in About a Week丨

Since the Legislative Yuan passed the Law on Secondary and Elementary Schools and the Ministry of Education announced it (previously named the Law on the Organization of Secondary Schools and the Law on the Organization of Elementary Schools, now the word "organization" has been removed, and named the Law on Secondary Schools and the Law on Elementary Schools, which is more concise than adding the word "organization"), the Ministry of Education immediately drafted the Regulations on Secondary and Elementary Schools based on the Law on Secondary and Elementary Schools passed by the Legislative Yuan (the law is a general outline, and the regulations are more detailed). The drafting of the Regulations on Elementary Schools has been completed, and the Minister of Education convened a departmental meeting on the 13th and 14th of this month with the secretaries, counselors, directors of the relevant departments, and related staff of the ministry to discuss it in detail. The Regulations on Elementary Schools have more than 70 articles, including considerable regulations and specific decisions on school administration and organization, the service and treatment of teachers and staff, the qualification of teachers, school holiday regulations, the examination of student performance, and curriculum equipment. All the articles have been generally approved and will be finalized after a final review. It is heard that the date of announcement will be in about a week.

Chen Burei Cautions Elementary School Teachers in Hangzhou

Make Up for Classes Missed Due to General Leave 170

Chen Burei, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education, stated that the elementary school teachers in Hangzhou took a half-day of general leave on the 10th of this month to petition the government for funds. This placed their own problems above the students' studies, which had a significant impact on the elementary school students. Moreover, elementary education in Hangzhou has a considerable reputation in the national education system, and this incident was a stain on Hangzhou's education. The municipal government has already notified the schools. It was found that the educational staff of the municipal elementary schools stopped classes for half a day to petition for the issuance of seniority pay, etc. This kind of action is regrettable because it interferes with the children's studies. In addition to ordering them not to repeat this in the future, they must make up for the missed classes before the end of this semester. This is an announcement.

The First District is Held Today at the Provincial High School

Hangzhou Municipal Government Stipulates Regulations for Substitute Pay for Maternity Leave for Female Elementary School Teachers

One Month of Leave Before and After Childbirth, the Municipal Government Pays the Substitute Teacher's Salary 173

The Education Section of the Hangzhou Municipal Government, in order to treat female elementary school teachers preferentially, has specially formulated the Regulations on the Payment of Substitute Pay for Maternity Leave for Female Elementary School Teachers in Hangzhou Municipal Elementary Schools, which was submitted to the Education Committee for approval on the 13th of this month. The regulations are recorded below: Article 1: The payment of substitute pay for maternity leave for female elementary school teachers in Hangzhou Municipal Elementary Schools shall be in accordance with these regulations. Article 2: Female teachers in municipal elementary schools may apply for maternity leave at the time of childbirth, one month before and after childbirth. After the principal submits a request to the municipal government for approval, the substitute teacher's salary will be paid by the municipal government. For the substitute teacher mentioned in the preceding paragraph, a resume, graduation certificate, and service certificate must be submitted for verification. Article 3: The payment method of substitute pay is as follows: A. The calculation of the substitute teacher's salary shall be submitted by the school to the municipal government for approval (excluding the spring vacation and summer and winter vacation dates stipulated by academic qualifications). B. After the substitute pay is approved, it must be submitted by the school for allocation after the substitute teacher's term of office expires and the teacher on maternity leave returns to school to cancel the leave. C. When the school applies for the allocation of substitute pay, it shall attach the substitute teacher's receipt. Article 4: If a female teacher submits a request for leave to the school after giving birth, substitute pay will not be given for the month before childbirth. Article 5: If the duties left by the female teacher during maternity leave are undertaken by the teachers in the school, substitute pay may not be requested. Article 6: For principals of municipal elementary schools who apply for maternity leave, only the substitute pay for the part of the duties they concurrently hold as a regular teacher will be allocated. Article 7: These regulations will be implemented after promulgation.

Local News

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education First Rectifies Municipal Schools 174

丨Director Pan Expresses His Political Views at the Memorial Week丨

Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, gave a speech at the bureau's memorial week yesterday (the 16th), recorded by Wang Daxu. The speech is as follows:

The first semester of this year is now coming to an end. I feel that I have many thoughts on the middle and elementary schools in this city. Let me briefly state them.

Because the end of the semester means the end of a stage, the Bureau of Education evaluates the performance of each municipal school for a semester at this time. Often during this period, many principals of municipal schools are quite uneasy. At the same time, on the other hand, there are many who hope to obtain a suitable position to serve, and they are also actively seeking opportunities. Therefore, some strange phenomena inevitably occur. From the perspective of educational administration, because the semester is coming to an end, the Bureau of Education rectifies the municipal schools and implements rewards and punishments. The purpose is to promote education, and it is completely based on the results of the bureau's usual inspections. However, if the handling is slightly improper, it may even lead to abuses and cultivate a habit and a widespread mentality that one must contact the staff of the Bureau of Education in order to become a principal and maintain one's position. When abuses occur, it will inevitably lead to school principals being unable to concentrate on running the school and spending most of their time running to the door of the Bureau of Education, and only spending a very small amount of time dealing with school affairs. In this way, how can the school have good performance? Even within the school, upon hearing that the principal may be changed, the faculty and staff are inevitably affected, their work is slackened, and the impact on children's studies is not insignificant. This kind of concept is actually wrong. It must be known that the bureau's evaluation of the performance of each school is based entirely on whether the principal and faculty of each school can fulfill their duties. Those with excellent performance should naturally be allowed to continue in their positions. Those whose performance is not well-managed will definitely not be corrected or reassigned due to their diligence in running around or the favors of one or two people. Sacrificing the students' studies cannot be tolerated. Therefore, among the principals of municipal schools, there are many who work very hard and have excellent performance. As long as they maintain their spirit of hard work and keep working hard, the bureau will naturally provide them with possible assistance. There is absolutely no need to cause unnecessary panic and disturbance at the end of the semester or school year.

The bureau spends 80,000 to 90,000 yuan of municipal funds every month. What exactly is it doing? Leaving aside the social education aspect, as for the school education aspect, it is nothing more than managing municipal schools and supervising private schools. At present, there are many private schools in this city that are not well-managed and should be banned. However, there are also those that are indeed well-managed and have achievements. As far as my personal feelings are concerned, I feel that to supervise private schools, we should start by rectifying municipal schools. If municipal schools have good performance, we should strive for further progress to serve as an example for private schools. If we neglect municipal schools and only want to strictly supervise private schools, it is really unreasonable. Because if the performance of municipal schools is poor, they will not only be unable to supervise private schools, but also lose the credibility of the bureau. During this period, the bureau should devote its full efforts to municipal schools. In the near future, as long as they do not violate educational laws and regulations, they should be given the opportunity to develop fully within the possible range. Those who are absolutely impossible to improve and are solely for the purpose of profit will naturally only be resolutely banned.

Secondly, local educational administrative organs should abide by all educational laws and regulations promulgated by the central government, needless to say. However, in many cases, it is also necessary to take into account local conditions and handle matters with discretion. Because of the vastness of our country, the differences in customs and local conditions, and the uneven level of knowledge of the people, it is practically impossible to achieve uniformity by marking a boat to find a sword. Even in terms of the situation and environment of this city, it is different from the inland areas. The level of English and arithmetic, due to the urgency of need, should be higher than in other inland areas. This is actually unnecessary to hide. Moreover, in terms of reason and logic, textbooks that are suitable for place A may not be fully applicable to place B. If the local educational administrative organs in all provinces and cities of China do not understand the way to exercise discretion and only know the methods determined by the ministry and cannot be flexible at all, then the situation of cutting the feet to fit the shoes will occur frequently, often causing the schools to flow into falsification and completely focus on superficial articles, turning into a kind of formalistic education. As far as my personal feelings are concerned, we should now turn around and pay more attention to substance. For example, the bureau's review of the academic qualifications of new students and transfer students in each school is a complex and time-consuming task. In fact, the result is only the discovery of some forged certificates and altered certificates. If we emphasize substance across the board, not just diplomas, and pay attention to the entrance examinations of each school, strictly ban schools that speculate for profit, and support the development of excellent schools, then all the schools that remain will inevitably be unwilling to accept students of average and poor quality in order to maintain their reputation. And students who want to succeed by luck, even if they have diplomas, must pass strict examinations before they can transfer. Then the diploma is equal to waste paper. The organization of forged certificates will naturally disappear. Schools that speculate for profit will be difficult to survive without being banned. Here, I am only talking about one aspect of the emphasis on form. Other aspects are too numerous to mention, causing educational administrative organs to spend the thoughts and talents of many people on meaningless forms, and there will be no progress in the substance of education. If this atmosphere of emphasizing form changes and an atmosphere of emphasizing substance is cultivated, then the future of education will definitely be optimistic. Therefore, I believe that the local educational administrative organs should take responsibility and handle all affairs within the scope of the central educational laws and regulations, taking into account local conditions, and not just adhere to the form on paper. We must use most of our energy to improve the actual practice of education, so that we can live up to the citizens of Shanghai.

I hope that the colleagues of the bureau will fully understand the policy of reforming the education of this city that I have put forward, starting with the rectification of municipal schools. If the municipal schools are all well-managed and have excellent performance, then strictly supervising private schools will definitely be twice the result with half the effort.

Curriculum Standards for Junior and Senior High Schools

The Municipal Bureau of Education Orders All Schools to Comply 175

The Municipal Bureau of Education of this city has recently received an order from the Ministry of Education to issue curriculum standards for junior and senior high schools, and has specially instructed all schools in the city to comply. The order from the Ministry of Education states that the provisional standards for the general curriculum of junior high schools and senior high schools were previously announced by the ministry in August and October of the 18th year of the Republic of China, respectively, and ordered the educational departments of each province and city to try them out. The trial period for these provisional standards has exceeded three years, and the ministry has collected trial reports from each province and city, and invited personnel actually engaged in secondary education to hold meetings to discuss and draft the official standards for each subject, and hired experts in each subject to review these drafts in detail and make final corrections to make them perfect. Except for a few subjects that need to be announced slightly later, the curriculum standards for physical education, Chinese, English, arithmetic, biology, chemistry, history, and music for senior high schools, and the curriculum standards for physical education, hygiene, Chinese, English, chemistry, botany, zoology, history, labor, and music for junior high schools have been finalized and announced by the ministry. It is urgent to send 20 copies of each subject's curriculum standards, which should be forwarded to the subordinate levels for compliance. This is an order.

The Shanghai Esperanto Society Restores

Correspondence School Enrolls Students Year-Round, Sets Up Lecture Classes in Different Districts for Face-to-Face Teaching 176

The Shanghai Esperanto Society, founded in 1908, is the earliest Esperanto organization in China. Over the years, it has organized various activities, such as the Esperanto Correspondence School, Green Light Magazine, and Esperanto Bookstore and Library, with remarkable achievements. At present, 90% of Esperanto scholars in the country are from the Esperanto Correspondence School affiliated with the society. Unfortunately, during the January 28th Shanghai Incident last year, the society was located in Zhabei and was completely destroyed, and has been suspended since then. Now, after the efforts of the society's founders, Lu Shikai, Hu Yuzhi, and Sheng Guocheng, it has been officially restored recently. A general meeting of members was held yesterday, and many important cases were discussed and decided, and Lu Shikai, Hu Yuzhi, Sheng Guocheng, Chen Zhaoying, Ba Jin, Lu Yan, Huang Jingwan, and others were re-elected as executive and supervisory committee members, as well as faculty and staff of the correspondence school, and lecture classes for face-to-face teaching were set up in different districts of this city. For detailed information, please contact the society at No. 30 Hualong Road, French Concession, 3rd Floor, or send a letter to Shanghai Post Office Box 1332.

Shanghai Basketball Association Diary: Donghua Athletes Guest Appearance 180

Seven Stars Forfeit, Yi Team Wins Without a Fight

Yao Guang Defeats Chen Team, 54-15

Special Mention

Hygiene Teaching Methods for Primary and Secondary Schools (3) - Lecture by Xu Suen, Recorded by Hua 184

Nutrition Teaching: Most schools in our country neglect the issue of nutrition.

It is no accident that most students look pale and thin. Foreign schools pay great attention to the nutritional quality of meals, treating dining halls as nutrition classrooms, teaching children how to eat and what to eat. When they see a child eating less, they will ask why to improve or treat the issue.

Hygiene Education Methods for Secondary Schools 185

Secondary school students are more difficult to manage than primary school students, but in some areas, they are also easier to teach. Hygiene education in secondary schools does not need to focus on trivial details but should instead focus on administration. Good administration will naturally lead to good hygiene conditions, while poor administration will cause hygiene conditions to deteriorate. From this, it can be seen that secondary school administration is a crucial key to hygiene education and should not be taken lightly.

The scope of hygiene education in secondary schools can be divided into three points: first, in-class teaching; second, integration with other subjects; and third, extracurricular activities. These will be discussed separately below.

In-Class Teaching Methods 186

Relying on textbooks, teachers teach, and students read. Who can't do that? However, repeating the mistakes of "teaching dead books," "teaching books to death," "teaching death," and "reading dead books," what good will it do? It should be known that hygiene teaching, in addition to textbooks, emphasizes training. But how easy is it to say training? Secondary school students have varying levels of understanding, and the curriculum is innovative, starting from the first year of junior high school, so problems arise one after another. The most fundamental difficulty is the source of good teaching materials. Only when the medical and educational communities work together in harmony can a solution be hoped for.

Past teaching materials first taught students to learn and memorize things like the skeletal and muscular systems, only making them feel burdened and not benefiting practical application. In the future, attention should be paid to relating teaching materials to students' lives. What benefit do students get from knowing how many bones are in the human body? Because this is irrelevant to life, it should be reformed as soon as possible. Issues of sexuality, the importance of cleanliness, prevention methods, and treatment skills are urgent and must be discussed and practiced before any progress can be made.

Interdisciplinary Teaching Methods 187

Studying hygiene diligently in hygiene class, but "discarding it like a worn shoe" in other subjects will still lead to the failure of hygiene education. Hygiene is related to the entire life, and based on the meaning of "education is life," it is not difficult to understand that each subject contains elements of hygiene. Due to time constraints, interdisciplinary teaching methods cannot be discussed in detail. Here are a few examples from mathematics: for example, calculating the comparative growth rate of bacteria, statistics on mortality rates for certain diseases, and finding the formula for certain drugs. As for biology, chemistry, and physics, there are even more opportunities to teach hygiene.

Extracurricular Teaching Methods 188

Extracurricular teaching methods focus on administrative matters, with environmental facilities being the most important issue. Some people, when they hear "facilities," immediately think of "economic difficulties," and thus, things that cannot be solved are resolved with these four words. It should be known that environmental facilities do not necessarily require money. Clean toilets, in addition to having running water and toilets, only require diligent cleaning to be hygienic. Conversely, if the school officials forget to supervise cleaning, even with excellent facilities, they will be filthy. A lot of money will be spent in vain. Mosquitoes and flies are everywhere, and spiderwebs are not swept away. I would like to ask, is it not economic difficulty? In short, environmental facilities do not need to have a "foreign" label. It is not considered respectable only if a lot of money is spent. Being able to rationalize is the best approach. Next, let's talk about medical facilities. Shanghai has a health bureau, and the bureau has a special school health section, which has been of great help in the progress of school hygiene education. However, teachers should use medical facilities. First aid skills, knowledge of ventilation, and the arrangement of teaching schedules all require special attention.

Hygiene education in high school is particularly important because students are approaching graduation. In the near future, they will become parents and enter society. Hygiene issues not only affect themselves but also others.

Secondary school students often nitpick and find fault with the school's shortcomings, which are often related to poor hygiene. They then use this as an excuse, and the school's reputation is completely lost. In such schools, it is impossible not to fall into a state of chaos. Therefore, how can school hygiene still be neglected? (End)
